2:22:1292:0:14:72:336:700:12:Times:12:Times:The Impact of Foreclosure Delay on U.S. Employment
2:23:1342:14:14:72:265:686:12:Times:12:Times:Kyle F. Herkenhoff and Lee E. Ohanian
2:24:1379:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:NBER Working Paper No. 21532
2:25:1407:14:14:72:150:658:12:Times:12:Times:September 2015
2:26:1421:14:28:72:165:644:12:Times:12:Times:JEL No. E24,J0,R3
2:27:1438:28:28:306:339:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:28:1446:28:14:72:540:588:12:Times:12:Times:This paper documents that the time required to initiate and complete a home foreclosure rose from
2:29:1543:14:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:about 9 months on average prior to the Great Recession to an average of 15 months during the Great
2:30:1641:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:Recession and afterward. We refer to these changes as foreclosure delay. We also document that many
2:31:1740:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:borrowers who are in foreclosure ultimately exit foreclosure and keep their homes by making up for
2:32:1838:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:missed mortgage payments. We analyze the impact of foreclosure delay on the U.S. labor market as
2:33:1934:14:14:72:540:518:12:Times:12:Times:an implicit credit line from a lender to a borrower (mortgagor) within a search model. In the model,
2:34:2034:14:14:72:540:504:12:Times:12:Times:foreclosure delay provides unemployed mortgagors with additional time to search for a high-paying
2:35:2131:14:14:72:540:490:12:Times:12:Times:job. We find that foreclosure delay decreases mortgagor employment by about 0.75 percentage points,
2:36:2230:14:14:72:540:476:12:Times:12:Times:nearly doubles the stock of delinquent mortgages, increases the rate of homeownership by about 0.3
2:37:2328:14:14:72:540:462:12:Times:12:Times:percentage points, and increases job match quality, as mortgagors search longer. Severe foreclosure
2:38:2427:14:14:72:540:448:12:Times:12:Times:delays, such as those observed in Florida and New Jersey, can depress mortgagor employment by up
2:39:2523:14:14:72:540:434:12:Times:12:Times:to 1.3 percentage points. The model results are consistent with PSID and SCF data that show that employment
2:40:2630:14:42:72:480:420:12:Times:12:Times:rates rise for delinquent mortgagors once the mortgagor is in the foreclosure process.
2:41:2716:42:14:72:166:378:12:Times:12:Times:Kyle F. Herkenhoff
2:42:2734:14:14:72:198:364:12:Times:12:Times:Department of Economics
2:43:2757:14:14:72:189:350:12:Times:12:Times:University of Minnesota
2:44:2780:14:28:72:141:336:12:Times:12:Times:kfh@umn.edu
2:45:2791:28:14:72:147:308:12:Times:12:Times:Lee E. Ohanian
2:46:2805:14:14:72:159:294:12:Times:12:Times:8283 Bunche Hall
2:47:2821:14:14:72:237:280:12:Times:12:Times:UCLA, Department of Economics
2:48:2850:14:14:72:131:266:12:Times:12:Times:Box 951477
2:49:2860:14:14:72:191:252:12:Times:12:Times:Los Angeles, CA  90095
2:50:2882:14:14:72:124:238:12:Times:12:Times:and NBER
2:51:2890:14:0:72:187:224:12:Times:12:Times:ohanian@econ.ucla.edu
3:52:2911:0:37:72:208:730:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:1    Introduction
3:53:2928:37:18:72:540:693:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Prior to the Great Recession,  the average time required to initiate and complete the pro-
3:54:3018:18:18:72:540:675:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:cess  of  home  foreclosure  in  the  United  States  was  about  9  months.   However,  foreclosure
3:55:3118:18:18:72:540:657:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:time rose substantially in many states beginning in the Great Recession.  A combination of
3:56:3208:18:18:72:540:639:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:housing policies, as well as delays due to the enormous increase in the number of delinquent
3:57:3300:18:18:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:properties being processed by courts and lenders, considerably increased the time of com-
3:58:3389:18:18:72:540:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:pleting foreclosure.  Policies include both state and national foreclosure moratoria, as well
3:59:3482:18:18:72:540:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:as the National Mortgage Settlement (also known as the “robo-signing” settlement) which
3:60:3569:18:25:72:243:567:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:permanently slowed foreclosures.1
3:61:3602:25:18:89:539:542:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:On average, the time to foreclose in the United States rose from about 9 months prior
3:62:3687:18:18:72:540:524:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to  the  Great  Recession  to  about  15  months  around  the  time  of  the  Great  Recession  and
3:63:3786:18:18:72:540:506:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:continued afterward.  As a result of these delays, the probability that a delinquent borrower
3:64:3879:18:18:72:539:488:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(hereafter referred to as a delinquentmortgagor)received a foreclosure notice, which is the
3:65:3970:18:17:72:540:470:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:initiation of the foreclosure process,  fell by one-third across all U.S. states.  Similarly,  the
3:66:4068:17:18:72:540:453:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:probability  that  a  delinquent  mortgagor  who  was  already  in  the  foreclosure  process  was
3:67:4166:18:26:72:514:435:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:evicted fell by one-third across all U.S. states.  We call these changesforeclosure delay.
3:68:4256:26:17:89:539:409:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This paper analyzes the impact of foreclosure delay on the U.S. labor market, with a focus
3:69:4346:17:18:72:540:392:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:on how this delay has qualitatively and quantitatively affected the labor market decisions
3:70:4436:18:18:72:540:374:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of unemployed mortgagors.  Two sets of statistics, which to our knowledge are new to the
3:71:4524:18:18:72:540:356:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:literature, motivate this study.  One statistic, which is presented and discussed in detail in
3:72:4618:18:18:72:540:338:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Sections 2 and3, is that the employment rate of persistently delinquent mortgagors is very
3:73:4708:18:18:72:540:320:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:low, but this rate increases when the mortgagors are in foreclosure and thus are at risk of
3:74:4799:18:18:72:540:302:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:losing their homes.  The second statistic, which is presented and discussed in detail in Section
3:75:4895:18:18:72:540:284:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:5,  is  that  many  of  the  mortgagors  who  persistently  miss  mortgage  payments  ultimately
3:76:4991:18:18:72:540:266:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:resolve their delinquency before foreclosure is completed.  This resolution is accomplished
3:77:5082:18:18:72:540:248:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:by the mortgagor making up for previous missed payments and late fees.  This process of
3:78:5169:18:18:72:540:230:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:successfully exiting delinquency/foreclosure is known ascuring.  Although curing has been
3:79:5258:18:18:72:540:212:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:discussed in the literature (seeAdelino et al.[2009]), the relative frequency of curing as well
3:80:5353:18:25:72:540:194:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:as the transitions out of delinquency to curing have not been documented to our knowledge.
3:81:5443:25:18:89:539:169:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The facts that (i) mortgagor reemployment rises as foreclosure becomes more likely, and
3:82:5530:18:18:72:540:151:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:that  (ii)  many  persistently  delinquent  mortgagors  ultimately  cure  lead  us  to  construct  a
3:83:5630:18:16:85:539:133:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:1See Gerardi et al.[2011] andCordell et al.[2013] for a summary of policies and a discussion of congestion
3:84:5736:16:0:72:409:117:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:which led to foreclosure delays during the 2007-2009 recession and afterward.
4:85:5814:0:18:72:540:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:search model of the labor market that includes homeownership, mortgages, and mortgage
4:86:5899:18:18:72:540:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:default with the possibility of curing.  We use this model to assess how foreclosure delay has
4:87:5993:18:18:72:540:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:had an impact on the level of employment among mortgagors since the Great Recession.  In
4:88:6081:18:18:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the model, unemployed households choose their search intensity, which affects the likelihood
4:89:6173:18:18:72:540:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of receiving a job offer that pays a stochastic wage, and they also choose a reservation wage.
4:90:6267:18:18:72:540:640:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Additionally,  households  choose  whether  to  default  on  their  mortgage  payment.   In  this
4:91:6364:18:18:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:model, foreclosure delay is an implicit line of credit between the mortgage lender and the
4:92:6454:18:18:72:540:604:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:borrower.  By defaulting on their mortgage payment, mortgagors open an implicit credit line
4:93:6545:18:18:72:540:586:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:with the lender that has a limited duration that depends on the time it takes to complete
4:94:6634:18:18:72:540:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure.  The credit line is closed either with the mortgagor curing or with a completed
4:95:6726:18:17:72:540:550:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure.  Foreclosure  delay  thus provides unemployed  mortgagors with additional  time
4:96:6818:17:18:72:540:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to search for a high-paying job.  However, as foreclosure becomes more likely, mortgagors’
4:97:6908:18:18:72:540:515:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:choices  regarding  search  intensity  and  their  reservation  wage  change  as  they  try  to  cure
4:98:7009:18:18:72:540:497:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and avoid eviction.  In the past, unemployed mortgagors would use cash-out refinancing to
4:99:7098:18:18:72:540:479:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:extract equity from their homes to smooth consumption (seeHurst and Stafford[2004]), but
4:100:7186:18:25:72:452:461:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:the cash-out refinancing market collapsed during the 2007-2009 recession.2
4:101:7260:25:18:89:539:436:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The  affect  of  foreclosure  delay  bears  some  similarity  to  the  impact  of  unemployment
4:102:7355:18:18:71:539:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:insurance.  Both of these mechanisms allow unemployed mortgagors to smooth consumption
4:103:7441:18:18:71:539:400:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:while searching for a good match (a high paying job).  Unemployment benefits and mortgage
4:104:7530:18:18:71:539:382:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure delay have two key differences,  however.  One is that the delinquent mortgage
4:105:7620:18:18:71:539:364:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:payments  ultimately  must  be  resolved  if  the  mortgagors  are  to  stay  in  their  homes.   The
4:106:7721:18:18:71:539:346:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:second is that the incentives to find a job near foreclosure for a mortgagor may be stronger
4:107:7813:18:18:71:539:328:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:than in the case of the expiration of unemployment benefits because of the implications of
4:108:7903:18:18:71:539:310:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure for (i) the cost of leaving the home and living elsewhere, (ii) the decline in credit
4:109:8000:18:25:71:489:292:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:access, and (iii) the potential deficiency judgment against a foreclosed mortgagor.
4:110:8083:25:18:89:539:267:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We conduct a quantitative experiment with three economies that are identical except for
4:111:8170:18:18:71:539:249:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:having different foreclosure timelines.  Each economy experiences the analogue of the Great
4:112:8261:18:18:71:539:231:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Recession with exogenously lower productivity, a higher rate of job destruction, and a lower
4:113:8353:18:18:71:539:213:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rate of job creation.  One economy has a 9-month timeline to foreclosure, which is the average
4:114:8447:18:17:71:539:195:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:prior to the Great Recession,  another has a 15-month timeline,  which is the U.S. average
4:115:8537:17:18:71:539:178:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:during and after the Great Recession, and another has a 24-month timeline, which is roughly
4:116:8628:18:16:85:539:160:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:2Hurst and Stafford[2004] estimate that during the recession, there were roughly 100 million homeowners,
4:117:8732:16:12:72:540:144:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:roughly 31 percent refinanced in 1993, and 18 percent of the homeowners who refinanced were unemployed.
4:118:8835:12:12:72:540:132:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:These refinances drew down roughly $16,000 of equity on average.  Appendix15documents the collapse of
4:119:8936:12:0:72:213:120:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:the cash-out refinancing market.
5:120:8969:0:18:72:540:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the average of the 10 longest foreclosure timeline states.  We then compute the solution to
5:121:9060:18:18:72:540:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the three models and measure unemployed mortgagor decisions regarding mortgage default
5:122:9146:18:18:72:540:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and curing, homeownership rates, delinquency, search intensity, their reservation wage, their
5:123:9239:18:25:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:employment level, and the average match quality, which is measured using the average wage.
5:124:9329:25:18:89:539:651:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Our  main  finding  is  that  the  increase  in  foreclosure  time  had  a  significant  impact  on
5:125:9428:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:mortgagor employment rates.  Specifically, we find that the employment rate for mortgagors
5:126:9518:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:is about 1.3 percent lower in the 24-month timeline and is about 0.75 percent lower in the
5:127:9608:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:15-month timeline economy compared with the 9-month timeline economy.  This impact of
5:128:9693:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure delay on employment is roughly comparable to extending employment benefits
5:129:9779:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:by 6 months and 4 months, respectively.  Foreclosure delays increase the stock of delinquent
5:130:9871:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:mortgagors by a factor of 2 but also allow more mortgagors to remain in their homes.  As
5:131:9959:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:a result homeownership rates rise by .3 percentage points with foreclosure delays.  We also
5:132:10050:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:find that match quality improves in the delay economies as the average wage rises, reflecting
5:133:10143:18:17:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the fact that unemployed mortgagors remain unemployed longer but on average find higher-
5:134:10231:17:26:72:134:472:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:paying jobs.
5:135:10243:26:18:89:540:446:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The  remainder  of  the  paper  is  organized  as  follows:  Sections2  and3  document  new
5:136:10334:18:17:71:539:428:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:facts about employment near foreclosure, Section4 describes the details of the foreclosure
5:137:10424:17:18:71:540:411:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:process,  Section5  explains  changes  in  transition  rates  into  and  out  of  default,  Section6
5:138:10524:18:18:71:540:393:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:describes the model, Section7 describes the calibration and steady state results, Section8
5:139:10614:18:18:71:539:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:includes the main foreclosure delay experiment, Section9 discusses the mechanism in light
5:140:10703:18:53:71:443:357:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of unemployment insurance and wage ladders, and Section10concludes.
5:141:10770:53:27:71:539:304:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:2    Mortgagor Employment Rates Rise during Foreclo-
5:142:10822:27:37:101:136:277:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:sure
5:143:10826:37:18:71:539:240:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This section presents data that are consistent with our theory by showing that employment
5:144:10915:18:18:71:539:222:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rates are higher for delinquent borrowers who are in foreclosure compared with delinquent
5:145:11004:18:18:71:539:204:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:borrowers who are not yet in foreclosure.  We use data from two surveys:  the Panel Study of
5:146:11096:18:18:71:539:186:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Income Dynamics (PSID) and the Survey of Consumer Finances (SCF). These data allow us
5:147:11181:18:17:71:539:168:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to track employment rates among mortgagors over various mortgage delinquency horizons.
5:148:11267:17:18:71:539:151:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The  data  show  that  employment  rates  among  delinquent  borrowers  are  roughly  constant
5:149:11361:18:18:71:539:133:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:as delinquency duration increases (e.g., delinquency increases from 60 days late to 90 days
5:150:11452:18:0:71:539:115:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:late), but the employment rate increases considerably when the mortgagor is in foreclosure.
6:151:11544:0:18:89:540:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The model economy developed in Section6 will interpret these data on the duration of
6:152:11628:18:18:72:540:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:delinquency, foreclosure, and employment as follows:  unemployed mortgagors will choose to
6:153:11718:18:18:72:540:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:miss  mortgage  payments  to  smooth  consumption  while  searching  for  a  job,  but  they  will
6:154:11816:18:18:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:then lower their reservation wage when losing their home through foreclosure is imminent,
6:155:11905:18:46:72:282:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and thus their employment rate will rise.
6:156:11946:46:33:72:216:612:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:2.1    PSID Evidence
6:157:11966:33:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We  use  data  from  the  2009-2011  PSID  Core/Immigrant  sample  and  the  2009-2011  PSID
6:158:12058:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Housing, Mortgage Distress, and Wealth Supplement to construct data on mortgagor em-
6:159:12142:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ployment rates and mortgage delinquency and foreclosure status.  The observations are for
6:160:12231:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:all working-age heads of household with mortgages.  The PSID collects data on delinquency
6:161:12320:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:status as of the survey date and whether the lender initiated the foreclosure process as of
6:162:12411:18:18:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the survey date.  We then separated these mortgagors into 5 bins according to their reported
6:163:12503:18:18:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:delinquency status:  (1) “No Missed Payments,” (2) “30 Days Late,” (3) “60 Days Late,”
6:164:12589:18:17:72:540:453:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(4) “90 or More Days Late,” and (5) “In Foreclosure,” and within each bin we classify their
6:165:12680:17:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:employment status as either employed or not employed.  In Appendix11, we also consider
6:166:12766:18:25:72:536:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the employment status of the spouse and find a similar patterns to the heads-only sample.
6:167:12855:25:18:89:539:393:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Table1 shows employment rates among mortgagors in these 5 mortgage payment statuses
6:168:12938:18:18:72:540:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:for  both  the  2009  and  2011  PSID.  Employment  rates  are  higher  for  those  in  foreclosure
6:169:13037:18:18:72:540:357:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:compared with those 90 or more days late for all categories except for the 2011 sample of
6:170:13126:18:18:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:mortgagors who are in states in which initiating foreclosure requires a court order, which is
6:171:13219:18:25:72:214:321:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:known as a “judicial state.”
6:172:13247:25:18:89:539:296:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We will show later that there are some statistically significant differences in employment
6:173:13337:18:18:72:540:278:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rates between delinquent mortgagors who are in the foreclosure process and thus at risk of
6:174:13427:18:18:72:540:260:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:losing  their  home  immediately,  and  delinquent  mortgagors  who  have  not  yet  entered  the
6:175:13524:18:25:72:456:242:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure process and thus have no risk of losing their home immediately.
6:176:13599:25:18:89:539:217:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:To estimate the impact of these 5 mortgage payment statuses on employment rates, we
6:177:13682:18:18:72:540:199:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:fit a linear probability model (LPM), a logit model, and a probit model of a{0,1}binary
6:178:13769:18:18:72:540:181:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:employment indicator on dummy variables for each of the 5 mortgage payment statuses.  We
6:179:13857:18:18:72:540:163:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:also control for variables that are often used in binary employment/unemployment regres-
6:180:13945:18:0:72:540:145:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:sions and which are also available in the PSID: previous income (measured as annual gross
7:181:14035:0:18:72:539:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:family income), unemployment duration, and liquid assets to income.3In addition, we also
7:182:14123:18:18:72:540:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:estimate regressions that control for compositional demographic differences.  Demographic
7:183:14212:18:18:72:540:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:controls include age, sex, marital status, and education.  To capture legal differences in the
7:184:14306:18:18:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure process across states,  we also control for whether or not the mortgagor is in a
7:185:14398:18:18:72:539:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:judicial state as described earlier, and whether or not they are in arecourse state, which is a
7:186:14493:18:18:72:540:640:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:state in which the borrower may be liable for losses suffered by the lender.  We describe the
7:187:14586:18:18:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure process in judicial states and recourse in detail in Section 4.  We conduct these
7:188:14679:18:25:72:515:604:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:compositional corrections using both a random effects and a fixed effects specification.
7:189:14767:25:18:89:539:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:These three approaches (LPM, logit, probit) are all used frequently in analyzing models
7:190:14854:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:with a binary dependent variable.  We therefore used all three approaches for completeness.
7:191:14945:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The LPM is cited as performing well in terms of unbiasedness and consistency if there are
7:192:15034:18:18:72:539:525:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:relatively  few  predicted  probabilities  that  lie  outside  of  the  unit  interval  (seeWooldridge
7:193:15136:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:[2010]  andHorrace  and  Oaxaca[2006]).   This  is  indeed  the  case  in  this  application,  with
7:194:15235:18:17:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:only 10 percent of predicted probabilities outside of the unit interval, and many of those are
7:195:15329:17:18:72:540:472:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:indeed very close to one.  The logit and probit specifications are also widely used and have
7:196:15421:18:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the benefit of restricting predicted values to lie in the unit interval.  However, the logit and
7:197:15517:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:probit  specifications  face  a  challenge  in  that  those  procedures  drop  all  observations  when
7:198:15619:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:using fixed effects for households that either never default or remain in default for the entire
7:199:15715:18:18:72:539:400:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:panel (2007-2009).4Since the logit and probit results are very similar, we only report the
7:200:15805:18:25:72:135:382:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:logit results.
7:201:15819:25:18:89:539:357:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The regression coefficients on the mortgage payment status indicators are used to con-
7:202:15905:18:18:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:struct a regression analogue to the data presented in Table1.  Specifically, Figure1 plots the
7:203:15999:18:18:72:540:321:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:statistics from that table, along with the regression constant plus the coefficients from the
7:204:16092:18:18:72:540:303:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:mortgage payment status variables from column (1) of Table2.  We use the random effects
7:205:16179:18:18:72:540:285:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:model for the compositional correction,  as the fixed effects specification results were very
7:206:16272:18:18:72:540:267:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:similar.  Figure1 shows that employment per capita is lower among defaulters, as one would
7:207:16362:18:18:71:539:249:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:anticipate.  However, note that employment increases for those in foreclosure, compared to
7:208:16452:18:18:71:539:231:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the other delinquency states.  Specifically, the employment rate for mortgagors in foreclosure
7:209:16546:18:18:71:539:213:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:is about 17 percentage points higher than it is for those who are 90 or more days late without
7:210:16640:18:17:71:540:195:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:correcting for demographics,  (Table2,  Column (2)),  and it is about 11 percentage points
7:211:16730:17:18:71:539:178:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:higher than it is for those who are 90 or more days late, after controlling for demographic
7:212:16821:18:19:71:248:160:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:differences, (Table2, Column (1)).
7:213:16855:19:15:85:539:141:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:3Here we use the PSID question that asks about checking and savings account balances, money market
7:214:16953:15:9:72:454:126:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:funds, certificates of deposits, Treasury securities, and other government savings bonds.
7:215:17042:9:0:85:363:117:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:4If included, those observations would have fixed effects of±∞.
8:216:17106:0:18:89:539:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Tables 2 and 3show the linear probability and logit regression statistics.  Using the linear
8:217:17198:18:18:72:540:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:probability  model,  we  find  that  in  both  the  random  effects  and  fixed  effects  regressions,
8:218:17300:18:18:72:540:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the employment rate is significantly different for households that are 90 or more days late
8:219:17391:18:18:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:versus households in foreclosure.  Households in foreclosure are more likely to be employed
8:220:17482:18:18:72:540:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:than  households  that  are  90  or  more  days  late,  controlling  for  composition.   In  the  logit
8:221:17585:18:18:72:540:640:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:specification,  employment per capita is significantly different from households that are 90
8:222:17677:18:18:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:or more days late versus those households in foreclosure for the fixed effect specification at
8:223:17771:18:18:72:540:604:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the 10 percent level.  However, the difference in employment in the logit specification with
8:224:17863:18:46:72:356:586:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:random effects is not significant at the 10 percent level.
8:225:17921:46:33:72:208:540:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:2.2    SCF Evidence
8:226:17940:33:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We  present  additional  evidence  on  foreclosure  and  employment  by  conducting  the  same
8:227:18034:18:18:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:analysis  as  earlier,  but  using  the  2007-2009  SCF  panel.   The  SCF  surveys  mortgagors  on
8:228:18133:18:18:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:their delinquency.  The responses allow us to classify them into one of three statuses:  “30
8:229:18225:18:17:72:540:453:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Days Late,” “60 or More Days Late,” and “In Foreclosure.” The “30 Days Late” and “60
8:230:18309:17:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:or More Days Late” statuses refer to mortgagors who are in default on any type of debt,
8:231:18396:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:including mortgage debt.  Thus, we do not know the specifics of their default.  However, our
8:232:18488:18:18:72:540:400:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:hypothesis that homeowners avoid foreclosure by lowering their reservation wage indicates
8:233:18577:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:that  the  SCF  mortgagors  should  also  have  higher  employment  in  foreclosure,  subject  to
8:234:18674:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:attenuation bias.  As in the PSID, the sample is all working-age heads of household with
8:235:18762:18:25:72:265:346:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:mortgages as of the 2009 survey date.
8:236:18799:25:18:89:539:321:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Figure2 is analogous to Figure1, as it plots the compositionally corrected LPM coef-
8:237:18883:18:18:71:539:303:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ficients  from  the  delinquency  status  indicator  variables  from  the  2009  SCF.5In  both  sets
8:238:18983:18:18:72:540:285:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of data,  even after  controlling  for compositional  differences,  there is  a significant increase
8:239:19083:18:18:72:540:267:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in  employment  during foreclosure  compared  with  being delinquent  but not  in foreclosure.
8:240:19177:18:18:72:539:249:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Table4 shows these results for both the linear probability model (Columns (1) and (2)) and
8:241:19267:18:18:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the logit model (Columns (3) and (4)).  The result that employment during foreclosure is
8:242:19355:18:18:72:540:213:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:higher than that in the “60 or More Days Late” category is statistically significant at the 5
8:243:19448:18:18:72:433:195:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:percent level in both the linear probability model and the logit model.
8:244:19519:18:15:85:539:177:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:5Mortgagors in the “30 Days Late” category are defined as those who reported being late on debt payments
8:245:19623:15:12:72:540:162:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:over the prior year, but never missing two or more months’ worth of payments.  Those who missed two or
8:246:19725:12:12:72:540:150:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:more months’ worth of payments over the prior year were counted as 60 or more days late.  Due to privacy
8:247:19829:12:12:72:540:138:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:issues, the state of residence is omitted from public use files.  Therefore, we are unable to include the controls
8:248:19943:12:0:72:386:126:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:for judicial/recourse states used in the previous analysis with the PSID.
9:249:20017:0:18:89:539:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Taken together,  data from the PSID and the SCF indicate that employment is higher
9:250:20099:18:18:72:540:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:among  foreclosed  homeowners  than  among  delinquent  homeowners  who  have  not  entered
9:251:20190:18:53:72:130:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure.
9:252:20202:53:37:72:450:641:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:3    Mortgage Delinquency as Implicit Credit
9:253:20246:37:17:72:539:604:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Missing  mortgage  payments  is  a  costlyimplicit  credit  line,  reflecting  late  fees  that  range
9:254:20348:17:18:71:539:587:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:from  3  percent  to  6  percent  per  month.   It  is  therefore  reasonable  to  expect  that  unem-
9:255:20450:18:18:71:539:569:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ployed mortgagors who do skip mortgage payments have likely exhausted lower-cost means
9:256:20536:18:25:71:376:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of smoothing consumption, such as using their other assets.
9:257:20595:25:18:89:539:526:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We indeed find that unemployed mortgagors who are delinquent have little or no liquid
9:258:20680:18:18:71:540:508:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:assets.   Figure3  shows  the  PSID’s  measure  of  liquid  asset  holdings  relative  to  income,
9:259:20778:18:18:71:539:490:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:for all heads of household with mortgages from the 2009-2011 PSID. Liquid assets include
9:260:20866:18:18:71:539:472:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:checking and savings account balances, money market funds, certificates of deposits, Treasury
9:261:20959:18:25:71:315:454:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:securities, and other government saving bonds.6
9:262:21006:25:18:89:539:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The graph splits liquid asset holdings into bins ranging from liquid assets between zero
9:263:21094:18:18:71:539:411:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to  5  percent  of  prior  annual  gross  family  income,  up  to  50  percent  or  more,  and  shows
9:264:21195:18:18:71:539:393:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:liquid assets for unemployed and employed mortgagors.  Note that 85 percent of unemployed
9:265:21284:18:18:71:539:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:mortgagors have exhausted or nearly exhausted their liquid assets, which suggests that they
9:266:21375:18:52:71:501:357:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:are indeed significantly constrained in being able to make their mortgage payment.7
9:267:21458:52:28:72:540:305:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:4    The Process of Mortgage Delinquency and Foreclo-
9:268:21511:28:37:101:136:277:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:sure
9:269:21515:37:17:72:540:240:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Before  presenting  statistics  on  mortgage  delinquency,  foreclosure,  and  curing,  we  provide
9:270:21614:17:18:72:540:223:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:some  background  information  on  the  actual  delinquency  and  foreclosure  process.   To  our
9:271:21711:18:18:72:540:205:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:knowledge, the model developed in this paper will include considerably more detail about
9:272:21799:18:18:72:540:187:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the  actual  features  of  the  delinquency  and  foreclosure  process  than  other  papers  in  the
9:273:21899:18:16:85:539:169:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:6The  PSID  definition  of  liquid  assets  does  not  include  stocks  or  bonds  outside  of  federal  government
9:274:22014:16:12:72:540:153:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:bonds.  Adding these measures to the PSID’s liquid assets does not change these results in any substantive
9:275:22120:12:8:72:91:141:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:way.
9:276:22124:8:16:85:539:133:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:7Gerardi et al. [2013] provide additional evidence that mortgagors who default are severely financially
9:277:22227:16:0:72:125:117:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:constrained.
10:278:22240:0:25:72:517:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:literature.  This detail will be qualitatively and quantitatively important for this study.
10:279:22331:25:18:89:539:705:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:Adelinquent borrowermeans that a borrower is 30 or more days late.  Anotice of default
10:280:22417:18:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:begins the process of foreclosure and is typically given to borrowers who are 90 or more days
10:281:22510:18:18:72:539:669:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:late.  Aforeclosure saleis conducted by auction, and anotice of saleis given one month prior
10:282:22602:18:18:72:539:651:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to the auction.  A borrower isevictedfrom the home after the sale.  A foreclosed borrower
10:283:22691:18:18:71:539:633:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:may be liable for adeficiency judgmentif the sales price is less than the mortgage balance.  A
10:284:22785:18:25:71:540:615:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosed borrower is ineligible for government-backed loans for 7 years (seeLowrey[2010]).
10:285:22877:25:18:89:539:590:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:There are two main types of foreclosures in the United States:  judicial and nonjudicial
10:286:22965:18:18:71:540:572:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(seeGhent and Kudlyak[2011] for state classifications).  To complete a judicial foreclosure,
10:287:23057:18:18:71:539:554:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the bank that owns the mortgage must sue the person living in the home in a state court.
10:288:23145:18:25:71:450:536:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A judge is required to rule on the case before a foreclosure sale can occur.
10:289:23221:25:18:89:540:511:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A nonjudicial foreclosure, also known as aforeclosure by power of sale, allows the bank to
10:290:23311:18:18:72:540:493:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:sell the house without a court’s approval.  A notice of default is sent to the mortgagor which
10:291:23405:18:18:72:540:475:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:explains that the bank intends to sell the property.  Typically, a sale will not take place for
10:292:23500:18:18:72:540:457:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:at least a month after receiving this notice.  Additional details about the foreclosure process
10:293:23595:18:46:72:226:439:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:are presented in Appendix17.
10:294:23623:46:33:72:314:393:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:4.1    Interest on Missed Payments
10:295:23657:33:18:72:540:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Mortgage payments are usually due on the first day of the month, and a late fee is typically
10:296:23749:18:18:72:540:342:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:assessed if the payment is not received within the first two weeks of the month.  The late fee
10:297:23843:18:18:72:540:324:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:is a fraction of the payment amount.  If the scheduled payment is $1,000 and the late fee is 3
10:298:23937:18:18:72:540:306:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:percent, then the mortgagor must pay $1,030 in the following month.  Most late fee interest
10:299:24028:18:52:72:489:288:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rates fall in the range of 3 percent to 6 percent per month (seeGoodman[2009]).
10:300:24107:52:27:71:539:236:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:5    Time  to  Foreclose  and  Transitions  In  and  Out  of
10:301:24167:27:37:101:206:209:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:Delinquency
10:302:24178:37:18:71:539:172:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In nearly all models with limited commitment and mortgages, missing even a single mortgage
10:303:24268:18:18:71:540:154:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:payment means that the mortgagor is evicted (seeGarriga and Schlagenhauf[2009],Cor-
10:304:24351:18:0:71:539:136:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:bae and Quintin[2009],Campbell and Cocco[2011],Chatterjee and Eyigungor[2011], and
11:305:24434:0:18:72:539:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Hatchondo et al. [2012]).8This common modeling assumption about the foreclosure process,
11:306:24522:18:18:71:539:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:however,  stands in contrast to two facts that will be relevant for analyzing the impact of
11:307:24613:18:18:71:539:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure  time  on  labor  market  actions:  (1)  default  is  protracted  and  typically  involves
11:308:24715:18:18:71:539:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:a borrower repeatedly missing  payments without  being evicted,  and  (2)  mortgagors often
11:309:24806:18:18:71:539:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:successfully exit the delinquency and foreclosure process by making up for missed mortgage
11:310:24896:18:25:71:127:640:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:payments.9
11:311:24906:25:18:89:539:615:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This section presents data that highlight two features of the actual foreclosure process.
11:312:24995:18:18:71:540:597:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:One is that many mortgagors who are in defaultself-cure,which means that the borrower
11:313:25080:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:makes up for missed payments plus penalties.  In fact,  even mortgagors who miss enough
11:314:25167:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:payments to enter the foreclosure process self-cure about as often as foreclosure is completed
11:315:25261:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(see  Pennington-Cross  [2010]).   The  other  key  feature  of  these  data  is  that  the  time  to
11:316:25362:18:25:72:385:525:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:complete foreclosure was much longer after 2009 than before.
11:317:25422:25:18:89:539:500:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Figure 5 presents data that summarizes the evolution of default, which includes missing
11:318:25509:18:18:72:540:482:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:payments, the foreclosure process, self-cure, and foreclosure completion.  These data are from
11:319:25603:18:18:72:539:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Lender Processing Services, Inc.  (hereafter called LPS – seeElul[2015] for a full description
11:320:25697:18:18:72:540:446:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of the data), which has compiled detailed mortgage data on roughly 2/3 of U.S. mortgages.
11:321:25786:18:25:72:450:428:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:LPS is one of two standard datasets that are used in mortgage analyses.10
11:322:25859:25:18:89:540:403:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Figure5 is a transition matrix which describes how mortgagors transit across mortgagor
11:323:25945:18:17:72:540:385:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:payment states.  The possible states are “current,” “60 Days Late,” “90 or More Days Late,”
11:324:26036:17:18:72:540:368:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:“In Foreclosure,” two measures of completed foreclosure (“Real Estate Owned” [REO] and
11:325:26122:18:18:72:539:350:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:“Liquidated”),  and  “Paid  Off,”  which  means  that  the  mortgagor  sold  the  home.11The
11:326:26214:18:18:72:540:332:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rows  are  the  beginning  states,  and  the  columns  are  the  ending  states.   The  period  is  one
11:327:26317:18:18:72:540:314:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:month.   The  table  includes  two  sets  of  entries:   the  black  entries  refer  to  the  transition
11:328:26421:18:18:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:matrix calculated from 2009-2011 data, in which foreclosure was significantly delayed, and
11:329:26511:18:16:85:539:278:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:8Our model is also related toKarahan and Rhee[2011],Hedlund[2011], andHead and Lloyd-Ellis[2012],
11:330:26608:16:12:72:540:262:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:who incorporate search in a model with housing,Herkenhoff[2013] andAthreya et al.[2014] who consider
11:331:26708:12:12:72:539:250:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:the way unsecured debt interacts with labor markets, andBenjamin and Wright[2009] andBenjamin and
11:332:26805:12:8:72:312:238:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Mateos-Planas[2011], who consider debt renegotiation.
11:333:26858:8:15:85:539:230:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:9The standard assumption that eviction is immediate also makes it difficult for models to match actual
11:334:26960:15:12:72:540:215:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:default rates.  Several authors use a period length of 2-4 years so that the discount rate is effectively small
11:335:27071:12:9:72:191:203:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:enough to generate default.
11:336:27098:9:15:81:539:194:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:10We use a sample of around 470,000 mortgages per year from LPS. This is a larger sample than used
11:337:27196:15:12:72:540:179:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:in other analyses of mortgages who use Core Logic, Inc., which typically range from 130,000 mortgages to
11:338:27300:12:9:72:316:167:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:400,000 mortgages (seeElul et al.[2010] among others).
11:339:27354:9:15:81:539:158:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:11We eliminated the “30 Days Late” state, since this state includes mortgagors who miss a payment simply
11:340:27458:15:12:72:540:143:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:as an error.  These errors include forgetting to send in a payment, mailing the payment late, the payment
11:341:27563:12:0:72:530:131:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:being lost in the mail, the payment being returned due to insufficient funds in a checking account, so on.
12:342:27671:0:38:72:519:730:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:the red underlined entries are for the 2001-2003 data.  Figure5 presents the following:12
12:343:27760:38:18:86:540:692:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:1.  Delinquency is often temporary, with frequent transitions from delinquent to current
12:344:27848:18:18:101:540:674:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(current means up-to-date on payments) and transitions resulting in a mortgagor be-
12:345:27931:18:18:101:540:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:coming closer to being current (i.e., the lower triangular entries for the states “30 Days
12:346:28021:18:27:101:408:638:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Late,”“60 Days Late,”and “90+ Days Late” are nonsparse).
12:347:28077:27:18:86:540:611:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:2.  Foreclosure,  which  we  define  as  the  time  between  the  delivery  of  the  default  notice
12:348:28177:18:18:101:540:593:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and eviction, is often temporary.  This means that there are frequent transitions out of
12:349:28265:18:18:101:540:575:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the foreclosure into curing.  Specifically, the probability that a mortgagor will success-
12:350:28355:18:18:101:540:557:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:fully exit foreclosure is about the same as the probability that a mortgagor who is in
12:351:28441:18:28:101:336:539:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure will suffer a completed foreclosure.
12:352:28489:28:18:86:540:511:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:3.  Entry into foreclosure is slow, and became slower after 2008.  Specifically, loans that
12:353:28580:18:18:101:540:493:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:were “90 or More Days Late” were in that category for 3.2 months on average during
12:354:28662:18:18:101:540:475:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the 2001-2003 period and 6.2 months on average during the 2009-2011 period.  The
12:355:28742:18:18:101:540:457:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:unconditional monthly hazard rate of receiving a foreclosure notice, after being 90 or
12:356:28828:18:17:101:540:439:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:more days late, dropped by 40 percent between the 2001-2003 survey and the 2009-2011
12:357:28912:17:28:101:352:422:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:survey, declining from 8.3 percent to 4.8 percent.
12:358:28962:28:18:86:540:394:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:4.  Foreclosure is a slow process, and became slower after 2008.  Specifically, conditional
12:359:29053:18:18:101:540:376:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:on reaching foreclosure, mortgagors remained in foreclosure on average for 4.0 months
12:360:29138:18:18:101:540:358:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:during the 2001-2003 period, and for 8.3 months in the 2009-2011 period. Consequently,
12:361:29224:18:18:101:540:340:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the unconditional monthly hazard of having a completed foreclosure, either as a bank-
12:362:29309:18:18:101:540:322:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:owned property, or as a liquidated property, dropped by 36 percent, declining from 8.6
12:363:29395:18:18:101:540:304:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:percent  in  2001-2003  to  5.5  percent  in  2009-2011.   The  increase  in  time  to  foreclose
12:364:29492:18:18:101:540:286:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:is concentrated among a group of states in which foreclosure delay rose substantially.
12:365:29578:18:18:101:540:268:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:These  states  include  California,  Florida,  Illinois,  Indiana,  Maryland,  Massachusetts,
12:366:29671:18:18:101:540:250:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:New Jersey, New York, Oklahoma, Pennsylvania, and Wisconsin.  Some other states,
12:367:29751:18:17:101:540:232:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:including Alabama, Arizona, Georgia, Iowa, Missouri, North Carolina, Oregon, Texas,
12:368:29834:17:28:101:530:215:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:Virginia, and Washington, did not experience a large increase in time to foreclose.13
12:369:29919:28:18:86:540:187:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:5.  Theself-cure probabilities, which we define as the lower triangular entries of the matrix,
12:370:30013:18:18:101:438:169:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:decreased in every single entry between 2001-2003 and 2009-2011.
12:371:30077:18:15:81:539:151:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:12This is a transition matrix, so in order to read this table, the rows are the starting state at the beginning
12:372:30188:15:12:72:540:136:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:of  the  month  and  the  columns  are  the  possible  states  next  month.   For  instance,  in  a  given  month  the
12:373:30306:12:9:72:509:124:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:probability of moving from being current to 30 days late is 1.7 percent during the 2009-2011 period.
12:374:30406:9:0:81:461:115:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:13See RealtyTrac [2012] for a detailed foreclosure timeline report and ranking of states.
13:375:30497:0:18:89:539:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In  summary,  these  data  show  that  (1)  there  is  considerable  movement  of  mortgagors
13:376:30590:18:18:72:540:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:across  different  levels  of  delinquency,  (2)  mortgagors  typically  spend  considerable  time  in
13:377:30692:18:18:72:540:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:mortgage  delinquency  before  entering  foreclosure,  (3)  foreclosure  takes  considerable  time,
13:378:30791:18:18:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(4) delinquent mortgagors often self-cure, and (5) the time spent in “90 or More Days Late”
13:379:30882:18:18:72:540:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and  “In  Foreclosure”  categories  rose  considerably  in  the  2009–2011  period,  and  the  self-
13:380:30982:18:18:72:540:640:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:cure probabilities declined during this period.  The model in the following section features
13:381:31074:18:18:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:a  delinquency  and  foreclosure  process  that  is  tailored  to  capture  these  features  described
13:382:31176:18:52:72:500:604:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:earlier, and is used to conduct an experiment comparing 2001-2003 with 2009-2011.
13:383:31257:52:27:72:540:552:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:6    Search Model with Persistent Mortgage Default and
13:384:31311:27:37:101:159:525:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:Curing
13:385:31317:37:18:72:540:488:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This section describes a model that features a labor search process with a reservation wage
13:386:31408:18:18:72:540:470:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:for unemployed agents and a housing market in which mortgagors can persistently default
13:387:31495:18:18:72:540:452:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:as well as exit default or exit foreclosure through repaying their delinquent balances.  The
13:388:31587:18:18:72:540:434:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:model is decision-theoretic in that the prices in the model are exogenous.  This simplification
13:389:31682:18:18:72:540:416:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:allows us to include substantial heterogeneity in the model in terms of individual employment
13:390:31775:18:18:72:540:398:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:histories, asset histories, and mortgage histories, while at the same time keeping the model
13:391:31867:18:18:72:540:380:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:tractable.  The analysis thus quantifies how the labor market is affected by changes in the
13:392:31958:18:25:72:234:362:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:time to foreclose, given prices.14
13:393:31992:25:18:89:539:337:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Unlike other papers in the literature, this paper allows mortgagors to self-cure by making
13:394:32082:18:18:72:540:319:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:up for missed payments, including late fees and accumulated interest.  To our knowledge, this
13:395:32175:18:18:72:540:301:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:is the first analysis that is consistent with the fact that delinquent mortgagors can self-cure
13:396:32270:18:25:72:371:283:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:within a model featuring mortgage finance and job search.
13:397:32327:25:18:89:539:258:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Time, indexed byt= 0,1,2,3,..., is discrete and runs forever.  The model economy is
13:398:32410:18:18:72:540:240:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:populated by a heterogeneous mass of risk-averse and finitely lived agents who are subject
13:399:32500:18:18:72:540:222:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to both idiosyncratic and aggregate shocks.  In each period, agents may participate in three
13:400:32592:18:25:72:431:204:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:markets:  the labor market, the asset market, and the housing market.
13:401:32661:25:18:89:539:179:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The  labor  market  features  search  frictions  similar  to  those  inLjungqvist  and  Sargent
13:402:32756:18:18:72:539:161:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:[1998]  andKrueger  and  Mueller[2010].   Unemployed  agents  exert  a  search  effortstat  a
13:403:32849:18:16:81:539:143:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:14It  would  be  interesting  to  try  to  extend  this  to  a  general  equilibrium  environment.   However,  this
13:404:32964:16:12:72:540:127:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:would complicate the solution of the model enormously, particularly in terms of the pricing of mortgages in
13:405:33071:12:0:72:540:115:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:conjunction with general equilibrium search and matching in the labor market.  We leave this to future work.
14:406:33181:0:18:72:539:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:utility costx(st) to increase the probability of receiving a wage offer.  Wage offers are drawn
14:407:33276:18:18:72:539:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:from an exogenous and stationary distributionF(·), and agents can reject or accept offers.
14:408:33366:18:18:72:540:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This  gives  rise  to  a  reservation  wage  profilew∗(·),  which  is  a  function  of  the  state  space
14:409:33471:18:18:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of the agent.  Once an offer is accepted and the agent is employed,  we consider two wage
14:410:33560:18:18:72:540:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:processes:  one in which the wage is constant for the duration of the match and one in which
14:411:33652:18:18:72:540:640:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the wage follows a Markov process.  The job match continues until it is terminated by an
14:412:33740:18:18:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:exogenous  and  stochastic  job  destruction  shock,  in  which  the  agent  becomes  unemployed
14:413:33836:18:25:72:268:604:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and then searches as described earlier.
14:414:33875:25:18:89:539:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In the asset market, agents can save (at>0) at a fixed risk-free rate  ̄rin order to smooth
14:415:33966:18:25:72:176:561:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:their consumption.15
14:416:33986:25:18:89:539:536:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In the housing market, homeowners can sell their homes, but once agents become renters,
14:417:34073:18:18:72:539:518:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:they are renters for the remainder of their lives as inCorbae and Quintin[2009]. Homeowners
14:418:34164:18:18:72:539:500:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:receive a flow utility from housing services given byzhand renters receive a flow utility of
14:419:34256:18:18:72:540:482:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:housing given byzrwherezr< zh.  In our model and similar to the model inChatterjee
14:420:34338:18:18:72:539:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and Eyigungor[2009], every homeowner has a mortgage perpetuity and must either make
14:421:34421:18:18:72:540:446:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the required payment or default.  The key difference in this model from existing models in
14:422:34511:18:17:72:540:428:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the literature is that both mortgage default and foreclosure are protracted and potentially
14:423:34602:17:26:72:489:411:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:reversible events, both of which influence job search and consumption decisions.16
14:424:34684:26:17:89:539:385:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Agents maximize discounted expected utility, in which preferences are defined over the
14:425:34770:17:9:72:540:368:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:expected stream of consumption of a nondurable good,c,housing services,zi,whereit∈
14:426:34852:9:9:72:79:359:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:{
14:427:34853:9:0:78:95:350:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:h,r
14:428:34856:0:9:96:103:359:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:}
14:429:34857:9:18:108:540:350:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f8:(hdenotes homeowner, andrdenotes renter), and search effort (if unemployed),s,
14:430:34935:18:18:72:539:332:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in whichx(s) is the disutility of searching andxis weakly increasing and is convex ins.We
14:431:35024:18:18:72:539:314:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:definêβ=  (1−pd)βas the death-adjusted discount factor wherepdis the probability of
14:432:35108:18:18:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:an agent dying andβis the household discount factor.  The household objective function is
14:433:35197:18:46:72:115:278:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:given by
14:434:35205:46:0:235:247:232:12:g_d0_f12:8:g_d0_f3:E0
14:435:35207:0:29:254:267:247:8:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f11:∞∑
14:436:35209:29:0:252:266:218:8:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f3:t=0
14:437:35212:0:0:271:280:235:12:g_d0_f11:8:g_d0_f9:̂βt
14:438:35215:0:10:280:285:242:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:(
14:439:35216:10:0:286:367:232:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f2:u(ct,zit)−x(st)
14:440:35231:0:10:367:372:242:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:)
14:441:35232:10:39:372:375:232:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:.
14:442:35233:39:18:89:539:193:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The model includes an aggregate shock that allows us to analyze the impact of foreclosure
14:443:35322:18:18:72:540:175:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:delay during the Great Recession.  We defineθtto be the aggregate state at datet, where
14:444:35409:18:16:81:539:157:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:15It  is  standard  in  defaultable  debt  models  to  take  the  risk-free  savings  rate  as  exogenously  given  (see
14:445:35529:16:8:72:336:141:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Eaton and Gersovitz[1981] orBenjamin and Wright[2009]).
14:446:35584:8:16:81:539:133:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:16This model is of the same general type explored in an earlier paper (Herkenhoff and Ohanian[2011a])
14:447:35685:16:0:71:337:117:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:where mortgage default does not necessarily lead to eviction.
15:448:35748:0:18:72:540:730:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f2:θtfollows a two-state Markov process,  in which it can be either high (H) or low (L).  As
15:449:35837:18:18:72:540:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:described in detail later, the aggregate state governs the job-finding rate, the job destruction
15:450:35933:18:25:72:187:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rate, and house prices.
15:451:35956:25:18:89:540:669:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:While  unemployed,  agents  search  for  a  job  with  search  intensity,st,  and  their  search
15:452:36052:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:disutility is given by (x(st)).  The probability of obtaining an offer, which we hereafter call
15:453:36147:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the job-finding probability, is a function of the aggregate state.  This is denoted asπ(st,θt)
15:454:36241:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and is increasing and concave inst.  Note thatπ(st,H)> π(st,L) for allst.  If the agent finds
15:455:36334:18:18:72:539:597:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:a job,  the wage offer is drawn from a stationary distributionF(w).  The agent can either
15:456:36423:18:18:72:539:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:accept or reject the job offer, which gives rise to a reservation wage profilew∗(·) that is a
15:457:36516:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:function of the state vector of the agent.  We denoteδ(θt) as the state-contingent probability
15:458:36610:18:25:72:316:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of a job being destroyed, in whichδ(H)< δ(L).
15:459:36655:25:18:89:539:518:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In  the  housing  market,  mortgages  are  modeled  as  perpetuities,  which  helps  keep  the
15:460:36749:18:18:72:540:500:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:model tractable.  When agents die, they are replaced by newborns, who are endowed with
15:461:36835:18:18:72:540:482:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:zero liquid assets and who are randomly assigned to homeownership, with fractionfmbeing
15:462:36922:18:18:72:540:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:endowed  with  a  home  (and  a  mortgage).   Newborn  agents  begin  with  wages  and  benefits
15:463:37018:18:25:72:408:446:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:drawn fromF(w).  A fraction 1−ubegin employed withu=.06.
15:464:37074:25:18:89:539:421:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Mortgages  have  a  constant  payment  per  period,ch,which  is  denoted  in  units  of  the
15:465:37166:18:18:72:539:403:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:nondurable consumption good.  The house price (p(θt)) is governed by the aggregate state
15:466:37254:18:17:72:539:385:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:such  thatp(L)≤p(H).   In  the  high  state,  the  price  of  a  home  is  given  asp(H)  =chrb,
15:467:37350:17:18:72:539:368:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:whererbis  the  fixed  mortgage  interest  rate.   In  the  low  state,  we  allow  potentially  for
15:468:37450:18:18:72:540:350:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:underwater  homeowners,p(L)≤chrb,  but  in  the  baseline  parameterization  we  will  assume
15:469:37543:18:47:71:258:332:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:thatp(H) =p(L) =chrbis constant.17
15:470:37577:47:32:72:401:285:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:6.1    Homeowner Delinquency and Foreclosure
15:471:37621:32:18:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This  section  describes  the  model  details  regarding  mortgagor  decisions  on  their  mortgage
15:472:37720:18:18:72:540:235:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:payment and whether they choose to sell the home.  Consider a mortgagor at datet.Mort-
15:473:37806:18:18:72:539:217:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:gagors are eithercurrent, which means that they are not delinquent on past payments, or
15:474:37893:18:18:72:539:199:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:they are indefault, which means that they are delinquent on at least one previous mortgage
15:475:37983:18:18:72:453:181:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f8:payment.  We denote the number of periods of delinquency at datetasnt.
15:476:38053:18:15:81:539:163:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:17As Mian et al.[2011] show, foreclosures may lead to house price declines, and thus foreclosure intervention
15:477:38162:15:12:72:540:148:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:may prevent negative equity.  We note that (i) since foreclosure delays may mitigate house prices drops, in
15:478:38269:12:12:72:540:136:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:order to avoid overstating the mechanism, we study delays in an environment in which house prices remain
15:479:38373:12:12:72:540:124:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:constant throughout the Great Recession and no agents are under water, and (ii) closing the housing market
15:480:38479:12:0:72:510:112:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:would require closing the mortgage market, and either of these tasks makes the problem intractable.
16:481:38580:0:18:89:540:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A  mortgagor  who  is  current  chooses  to  either  (i)  make  the  datetmortgage  payment
16:482:38671:18:18:71:539:712:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f2:ch,(ii) miss the datetmortgage paymentch, or (iii) sell the house.  A mortgagor who is in
16:483:38760:18:18:71:539:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:default chooses to either (i) make the two most delinquent payments, including penalties, (ii)
16:484:38854:18:18:71:540:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:continue in default by missing the datetpayment, or (iii) sell the house.  A mortgagor who
16:485:38944:18:18:71:539:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:is delinquent risks foreclosure, which means that the mortgagor is evicted from the home.  A
16:486:39036:18:18:71:539:640:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:delinquent mortgagor can temporarily stop foreclosure by making two delinquent payments,
16:487:39124:18:18:71:539:622:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:including the penalty interest payment.  If a delinquent mortgagor does this in period t, but
16:488:39217:18:18:71:540:604:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:has remaining unpaid mortgage payments in periodt+ 1, the mortgagor must make another
16:489:39302:18:25:71:514:586:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:two mortgage payments int+ 1 in order to stop the foreclosure process for datet+ 1.
16:490:39385:25:18:89:539:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:For simplicity, the mortgagor must pay thetwo  longest  outstanding  mortgage  payments
16:491:39472:18:18:71:539:543:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f2:with penalty interest((1 +rb)n−1ch+ (1 +rb)nch), whererbis the penalty interest rate.  This
16:492:39563:18:18:71:540:525:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:feature of the model is consistent with the fact that the empirical transitions in Figure5
16:493:39653:18:18:71:539:507:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:show that homeowners slowly transit out of delinquency, rather than curing immediately by
16:494:39742:18:17:71:539:489:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:making good on all missed payments and penalties.  Moreover, the assumption in our model
16:495:39830:17:18:71:539:472:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:that initiation of mortgagor self-curing stops the foreclosure process is consistent with the
16:496:39923:18:26:71:480:454:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:fact that lenders prefer receiving late fees to foreclosure (seeThompson[2010]).
16:497:40003:26:17:89:539:428:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A delinquent mortgagor is able to smooth consumption by missing a payment, but risks
16:498:40087:17:18:72:539:411:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure.  The time to foreclosure is governed by the functionλF(nt), which denotes the
16:499:40177:18:18:72:540:393:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:probability of foreclosure as a function of the number of missed payments by the mortgagor.
16:500:40268:18:18:72:539:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:As the time spent in default (nt) increases, the probability of foreclosure increases:λF(n)≤
16:501:40360:18:18:72:539:357:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f2:λF(n′)∀n′> n(see Figure4 for the foreclosure probability for (A) the 9-month timeline,
16:502:40446:18:18:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(B) the 15-month timeline,  and (C) the 24-month timeline).  If the homeowner sells or is
16:503:40535:18:18:72:540:321:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosed upon, they become permanent renters.  The mortgage payment is greater than the
16:504:40624:18:18:72:539:303:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rental payment (ch> cr), but the utility flow from owning a home strictly dominates the
16:505:40711:18:18:72:539:285:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:utility flow from renting (zh> zr).  The rental payment is set to zero such that the renter
16:506:40802:18:18:72:540:267:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:with the lowest possible unemployment benefits given bybcan consume at leastc=b, where
16:507:40888:18:25:72:221:249:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f2:cis subsistence consumption.
16:508:40916:25:18:89:539:224:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:To model the possibility of a deficiency judgment against a foreclosed mortgagor, a fore-
16:509:41005:18:18:72:539:206:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:closed house is sold at a discount of 1−χ.  For example, ifχ=.95, this corresponds to a
16:510:41092:18:18:72:540:188:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:5 percent discount and the house is sold forχ·p(θt).  For homes sold at a loss,G(·) is a
16:511:41180:18:18:71:539:170:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:function which describes the potential deficiency judgment owed by the ex-homeowner as a
16:512:41268:18:25:71:254:152:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:function of the proceeds of the sale.
16:513:41305:25:0:89:539:127:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The unique focus of this model is that prolonged mortgage default will have an impact
17:514:41392:0:18:72:540:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:on the labor market by affecting the reservation wage and search effort of an unemployed
17:515:41480:18:18:72:540:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:homeowner.  Specifically, initial default will be associated with a low foreclosure probability,
17:516:41576:18:18:72:540:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:which means that agents will have a relatively high reservation wage and may also economize
17:517:41667:18:18:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:on  their  search  effort.   As  foreclosure  becomes  more  likely,  search  effort  will  rise  and  the
17:518:41773:18:46:72:221:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:reservation wage will decline.
17:519:41803:46:33:72:301:612:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:6.2    Employed Discrete Choices
17:520:41835:33:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We focus on the recursive representation of the maximization problems for the agents, so we
17:521:41926:18:17:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:will now drop time subscripts and use primes to denote the datet+ 1 value.  We denote value
17:522:42017:17:18:72:540:544:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:functions associated with a discrete choice with a tilde, e.g., ̃W.  We begin with employed
17:523:42108:18:18:72:540:526:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:agents. The value function for the discrete choice faced by an employed homeowner with wage
17:524:42199:18:18:72:539:508:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:w, liquid assetsa, with no late payments (n= 0), and in aggregate stateθis ̃Wh(w,a,0;θ).

17:526:42376:18:18:71:539:472:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and face the risk of foreclosure (Wdh(w,a,0;θ)), or sell the home (Wsh(w,a,0;θ)).  Thus, the
17:527:42468:18:30:71:326:454:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:value of entering the period in current standing is
17:528:42519:30:10:109:240:424:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f2: ̃Wh(w,a,0;θ) =max
17:529:42537:10:0:192:266:414:8:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f9:Pay, Default, Sell

17:534:42596:41:18:89:539:380:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Whenn≥1, the mortgagor has missednpayments and owes the lender a minimum of

17:547:43208:46:32:72:297:162:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:6.3    Employed Value Functions
17:548:43239:32:18:72:540:130:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We  begin  with  renters.   An  employed  renter  with  wagewand  liquid  assetsahas  value

18:559:43826:0:10:500:505:653:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:]

18:563:43859:33:18:89:540:559:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:An  employed  homeowner  with  wagew,  liquid  assetsa,  current  paymentsn=  0,  and

23:889:52387:18:34:71:281:279:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for any interior points of the state space.
23:890:52430:34:28:71:198:245:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f2:Proof.See Appendix14.
23:891:52451:28:18:72:539:217:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f4:Lemma 6.2.Consider  a  version  of  the  model  that  satisfies  the  hypothesis  of  Lemma6.1.

26:967:57593:0:18:89:540:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The flow utility of renting,zr, can be normalized and is set to one.  The cost of renting

26:972:58034:25:18:89:539:633:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The foreclosure completion probability functionλF(n) is piecewise linear, which allows
26:973:58120:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:us to approximate the distribution of actual foreclosures.  Specifically, this function captures
26:974:58216:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the fact that time to foreclose is stochastic and becomes certain after a sufficient number of
26:975:58310:18:51:72:177:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:periods have passed:
26:976:58330:51:0:241:283:528:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f2:λF(n) =
26:977:58337:0:11:287:298:553:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:
26:978:58338:11:21:287:298:542:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:
26:979:58339:21:0:287:298:521:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:
26:980:58340:0:22:297:365:538:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:fc,ifn≤N
26:981:58348:22:31:297:369:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f8:1,ifn > N.
26:982:58358:31:18:89:540:485:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Specifically, households are evicted with probabilityfcbetween periodnandN,which is
26:983:58441:18:17:71:539:467:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:chosen to match the transition rate from the process of foreclosure to completed foreclosure
26:984:58533:17:18:71:539:450:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in Figure5.  After monthN, households are evicted with certainty.  In addition to matching
26:985:58623:18:18:71:539:432:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the foreclosure completion transition rate, this process also captures other empirical features
26:986:58718:18:25:71:414:414:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of the delinquency and foreclosure process which is described later.
26:987:58786:25:18:89:539:389:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We analyze three specifications of foreclosure time. The first has a foreclosure timeline of 9
26:988:58880:18:18:71:539:371:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:months (N= 9),which corresponds to the modal number of days from default to foreclosure
26:989:58967:18:18:71:540:353:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:sale  as  outlined  by  Fannie  Mae  and  Freddie  Mac.22In  addition,  a  few  foreclosures  occur
26:990:59066:18:18:71:539:335:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:beforeNperiods, sofcwill be about 3 percent in order to capture this fact.  The second
26:991:59152:18:18:71:540:317:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure timeline is 15 months (N= 15), which is a nationally representative foreclosure
26:992:59243:18:18:71:540:299:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:timeline from LPS data for 2009-2011 (see Figure5).  The third foreclosure timeline is based
26:993:59335:18:18:71:539:281:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:on the most extreme observed foreclosure delays, which is about 24 months in Florida and
26:994:59423:18:18:71:540:263:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:New Jersey.  Although the foreclosure completion probability functionλF(n) is stylized, it
26:995:59513:18:18:71:539:245:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:enables the model to roughly approximate many of the observed transitions across mortgage
26:996:59602:18:25:71:151:227:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:payment states.
26:997:59617:25:18:89:539:202:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The foreclosure discount on the sale price of the home is 22 percent (χ=.22),  which
26:998:59701:18:18:71:539:184:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:corresponds to the average reported byPennington-Cross[2006].  A deficiency judgment on
26:999:59788:18:18:71:539:166:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosed homes is equal to the amount owed times the observed deficiency enforcement rate.

27:1008:60416:33:18:72:540:610:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The model deficiency judgment does not distinguish between recourse and nonrecourse states.
27:1009:60507:18:17:72:540:592:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This is because states that are often considered to be nonrecourse states can have recourse

27:1027:62020:25:18:89:539:248:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:To measure debt, we calculate average back-end debt-to-income ratios in the PSID. The

27:1030:62284:18:18:72:540:194:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Since these other obligations are not in our model, but since they do impact ability to pay,
