27:1033:62560:16:12:72:540:143:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:– Occupied Units:  2007”, which provides data on nearly 76 million owner-occupied housing units.  The data
27:1034:62666:12:12:72:540:131:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:on homeownership is from Census Table 5.  “Homeownership Rates for the United States and Regions:  2006
27:1035:62769:12:0:72:112:119:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:to 2012”.
28:1036:62780:0:18:72:540:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:applying the NBER’s TAXSIM program to the 2009 PSID dataset to generate after-tax in-
28:1037:62865:18:18:72:540:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:come.24From the after-tax income, we further subtract insurance expenses, lease outlays,
28:1038:62953:18:18:72:540:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and  an  imputed  unsecured  debt  service  flow  equal  to  14.31  percent  of  the  stock  of  unse-
28:1039:63055:18:18:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:cured debt (14.31 percent is the average credit card interest rate taken from the 2009 Flow
28:1040:63146:18:18:72:540:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of Funds).  The ratio of mortgage payments, including first and second mortgages, to this
28:1041:63235:18:18:72:540:640:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:adjusted after-tax income number is what we will call the back-end debt-to-income ratio.
28:1042:63323:18:25:72:234:622:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:Table 5 tabulates these ratios.25
28:1043:63356:25:18:89:539:597:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The  ergodic  unemployment  rate  that  we  will  target  is  6.5  percent.26The  cure  rates
28:1044:63449:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:are taken to be the lower triangular entries in Figure5, summed across columns to yield a
28:1045:63538:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:model-equivalent measure.  We target the cure rate from 60 days late (DL) to current and
28:1046:63626:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:from 90 days late to 60 days late.  Liquid assets are measured as in Section3 and depicted in
28:1047:63719:18:18:71:540:525:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Figure3.  We target the fraction of homeowners with liquid assets to annual income between
28:1048:63809:18:46:71:154:507:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:0 and 5 percent.
28:1049:63825:46:33:71:435:461:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:7.2    Model Statistics Compared with Data Targets
28:1050:63875:33:18:71:539:428:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Since the model has more targets than parameters, we chose parameters by minimizing the
28:1051:63962:18:17:71:539:410:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:sum of squared deviations between the model and the data statistics.  Table6 shows that
28:1052:64049:17:18:71:539:393:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the calibration does reasonably well in approximating these targets.  Defaulters have back-
28:1053:64140:18:18:71:539:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:end debt-to-income ratios in line with the data, and the mortgagor unemployment rate is
28:1054:64227:18:25:71:511:357:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:identical to the data.  Defaulters also have similar liquid asset holdings as in the data.
28:1055:64317:25:18:89:540:332:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:As is standard in any default model, it is necessary to have a high discount rate:  theβin
28:1056:64407:18:18:71:540:314:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the model corresponds to an annual discount rate of roughly 16 percent.27The bank interest
28:1057:64497:18:18:71:539:296:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rate corresponds to an annual rate of 5.8 percent, and the savings rate corresponds to an
28:1058:64586:18:18:71:539:278:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:annual yield of 1.08 percent.  These interest rates primarily determine the cure rate and the
28:1059:64679:18:18:71:539:260:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:fraction of liquid assets held by homeowners, respectively.  The cure rate is quite high in the
28:1060:64774:18:18:71:539:242:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:data, even during the recession, and thus the bank fees must be low.  Note that by omitting
28:1061:64865:18:18:71:539:224:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:mortgage modifications, we may be biasing downward the bank penalty rate, since a large
28:1062:64952:18:15:81:539:206:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:24TAXSIM  is  a  program  made  by  the  NBER  specifically  for  computing  tax  liabilities.   As  in  any  tax
28:1063:65065:15:12:72:540:191:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:return, TAXSIM takes as inputs the marital status in filing, exemptions, and deductions, including mortgage
28:1064:65172:12:9:72:455:179:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:deductibles, etc.  TAXSIM then yields the federal and state tax liabilities of households.
28:1065:65262:9:15:81:539:170:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:25In the event that a household had negative income after these adjustments, we dropped them from the
28:1066:65363:15:9:72:316:155:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:sample, thus understating the burden of mortgage debt.
28:1067:65417:9:15:81:539:146:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:26Our model has no participation margin and thus the unemployment rate in our model corresponds to a
28:1068:65517:15:9:72:167:131:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:number more like U6.
28:1069:65537:9:0:81:432:122:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:27The discount rate cannot be too high since it also shifts the asset distribution.
29:1070:65622:0:25:72:509:730:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:number of homeowners have had their mortgages modified or had late fees forgiven.28
29:1071:65705:25:18:89:539:705:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In this calibration, the model does not generate home sales except through foreclosure.
29:1072:65792:18:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:However, this feature of the calibration may not be important, as home sales were very low
29:1073:65882:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:during this period, falling by a factor of eight (see Figure5).  The search disutility parameter
29:1074:65978:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:is set to match the 6.5 percent ergodic unemployment rate; however, the disutility of search
29:1075:66070:18:53:72:417:633:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:parameter also indirectly affects the mortgagor rate and cure rates.
29:1076:66138:53:36:72:540:580:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:8    Impact of Foreclosure Delay during Great Recession
29:1077:66193:36:18:72:540:544:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This section quantifies the impact of the large increased time to foreclosure that occurred
29:1078:66284:18:18:72:540:526:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:during the Great Recession.29Our approach is as follows.  We take three identical economies
29:1079:66375:18:18:72:540:508:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:with the 9-month foreclosure timeline and which had been in the high aggregate state for the
29:1080:66467:18:18:72:540:490:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:preceding 12 months.  All three economies next enter the low state,θ=L, and remain in that
29:1081:66557:18:18:72:540:472:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:state for 18 months, which is about the length of the Great Recession as defined by the NBER
29:1082:66649:18:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(December 2007 to June 2009).  At the onset of the low state, one economy continues with
29:1083:66737:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the 9-month foreclosure timeline, and we call this the “no delay economy.” The foreclosure
29:1084:66827:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:timeline in the second of the economies increases to 15 months, which corresponds to the
29:1085:66915:18:18:72:540:400:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:national average, and we call this the “foreclosure delay economy.” The foreclosure timeline
29:1086:67007:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in the third of the economies increases to 24 months, which is roughly the average foreclosure
29:1087:67101:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:time for the 10 most delayed states, such as Florida, California, and New York.  We call this
29:1088:67194:18:18:72:540:346:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the “long foreclosure delay economy.” Thus, the only difference between the three economies
29:1089:67285:18:18:72:540:328:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:is that one has a 9-month foreclosure timeline, one has a 15-month foreclosure timeline, and
29:1090:67377:18:25:72:279:310:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:one has a 24-month foreclosure timeline.
29:1091:67417:25:18:89:540:285:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Figure4 plots how the probability of foreclosure depends on the number of months in
29:1092:67500:18:18:71:539:267:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:default.   In  the  no  delay  economy,  there  is  a  constant  foreclosure  rate  of  3.02  percent  for
29:1093:67606:18:17:71:539:249:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:borrowers who are delinquent between 1 and 8 months, and certain eviction occurs in the
29:1094:67693:17:18:71:539:232:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:9th  month.   Recall  that  we  chose  the  3.02  percent  eviction  rate  to  account  for  the  small
29:1095:67796:18:18:71:539:214:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:number of early foreclosures that do occur in the data.  In the delay economy, there is also a
29:1096:67890:18:18:71:539:196:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:constant foreclosure rate of 3.02 percent for borrowers who are delinquent between 1 and 14
29:1097:67981:18:16:81:539:178:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:28In  a  working  paper  version  of  the  model  we  include  modifications  as  a  random  event  that  competes
29:1098:68095:16:12:72:539:162:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:with foreclosure.  Including means tested modifications distorts job taking behavior even more.  SeeMulligan
29:1099:68203:12:8:72:303:150:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:[2008] andHerkenhoff and Ohanian[2011a] for more.
29:1100:68252:8:16:81:540:142:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:29This experiment relates to work byMulligan[2008,2010,2011] andHerkenhoff and Ohanian[2011b]
29:1101:68345:16:12:71:539:126:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:who study the way various government housing policies, including mortgage modifications, have increased
29:1102:68448:12:0:71:346:114:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:unemployment by distorting incentives to find and accept jobs.
30:1103:68512:0:18:72:540:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:months, and certain eviction occurs in the 15th month.  There is an analogous process for
30:1104:68601:18:25:72:463:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the long foreclosure delay economy, with certain eviction in the 24th month.
30:1105:68677:25:18:89:539:687:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The job-finding rate and the job destruction rate during the Great Recession were quite
30:1106:68764:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:different  from  those  in  previous,  milder  recessions.   We  therefore  adjust  the  model’s  job-
30:1107:68866:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:finding and job destruction rates, using data from JOLTS. We find that the job-finding rate
30:1108:68957:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:fell by about 37 percent and that the job destruction rate rose by about 27 percent between
30:1109:69048:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:2007 to 2009.  Table 7 summarizes the impact of the 2007-2009 recession on job-finding and
30:1110:69138:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:layoff rates in the data.  To capture the severity of the Great Recession,  we unexpectedly
30:1111:69229:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:reduce  job  offers  and  increase  job  destruction  rates  during  the  18  months  for  which  the
30:1112:69330:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:economy is in the low aggregate state.  Specifically, the job-finding rate in the low state is
30:1113:69424:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:adjusted down fromαf(L) =.76 to.64.Similarly, the job destruction rate in the low state,
30:1114:69512:18:25:71:331:525:12:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f3:δ(L), is adjusted from 1.5 in the low state to 1.7.30
30:1115:69565:25:18:89:539:500:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:At the end of 18 months in the low state,  both economies enter the high state,  which
30:1116:69651:18:18:71:539:482:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:continues thereafter, and in which job destruction and job creation rates return to their high
30:1117:69745:18:25:71:316:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:state levels, and the time to foreclose continues.
30:1118:69795:25:38:89:332:439:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The main experiment is summarized as follows:
30:1119:69840:38:18:89:540:401:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f2:•Both economies are identical, including the 9-month foreclosure timeline, had been in
30:1120:69926:18:18:101:540:383:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the aggregate high state for the previous 12 months, and before that had been in the
30:1121:70010:18:28:101:206:365:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ergodic steady state.
30:1122:70031:28:30:89:133:337:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f8:•Datet
30:1123:70037:30:18:114:540:307:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f2:–Both  economies  enter  the  low  state  for  18  months.   The  job  destruction  rate
30:1124:70125:18:18:127:540:289:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and  the  job  creation  rate  are  modified  as  described  earlier  to  capture  the  job
30:1125:70216:18:23:127:471:271:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:destruction and job creation that occurred between 2007 and 2009.
30:1126:70281:23:18:114:540:248:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f2:–One economy introduces default protection through a 15-month foreclosure time-
30:1127:70360:18:18:127:540:230:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:line,  which  we  call  the  foreclosure  delay  economy,  whereas  the  other  economy
30:1128:70447:18:18:127:529:212:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:maintains a 9-month foreclosure timeline, which we call the no delay economy.
30:1129:70524:18:16:81:539:194:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:30We choose to set the Great Recession job destruction and job creation rates as unexpected events based
30:1130:70628:16:11:72:539:178:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:on  forecasts  that  the  economy  would  recover  much  more  quickly  than  it  did.   Specifically,Romer[2009]
30:1131:70741:11:12:72:540:167:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:forecast a relatively quick recovery in the labor market.Sahm[2015] documents economic forecasts during
30:1132:70844:12:12:72:540:155:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:the Great Recession and finds that FOMC forecasts significantly overpredicted GDP growth in 2009 and 2010.
30:1133:70950:12:12:72:540:143:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Specifically, she reports that the forecasted GDP growth for 2009 and 2010 was much stronger than actual
30:1134:71054:12:12:72:539:131:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:growth, and that unemployment would be in the range of 6.6 percent to 7.5 percent in 2011 (seeSahm[2015]
30:1135:71158:12:0:72:522:119:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:andhttp://www.federalreserve.gov/monetarypolicy/files/FOMC20090128SEPcompilation.pdf).
31:1136:71246:0:18:89:539:730:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f2:•Datet+ 18:  Both economies enter the high aggregate state (θ=H) and remain there.
31:1137:71328:18:46:101:336:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Each economy maintains its time to foreclose.
31:1138:71373:46:33:72:540:666:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:8.1    Model Transitions In and Out of Delinquency and Foreclosure
31:1139:71439:33:18:72:539:633:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:To illustrate how foreclosure delay affects defaulting and curing, Figure 6presents the transi-
31:1140:71534:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:tion matrix across mortgage payment states for the no delay economy and for the foreclosure
31:1141:71625:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:delay economy from this experiment.  The black numbers are for the foreclosure delay econ-
31:1142:71715:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:omy, and the red underlined numbers are for the no-delay economy and are thus interpreted
31:1143:71804:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:as the counterfactual.  For simplicity, note that the model transition matrix does not include
31:1144:71898:18:25:72:401:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:as many states as the empirical transition matrix from Figure5.
31:1145:71961:25:18:89:539:518:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We focus on two features of these model statistics.  The first is that the model approxi-
31:1146:72050:18:18:72:540:500:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:mately captures the impact of foreclosure delay, as the probability of a borrower who is in
31:1147:72141:18:18:72:540:482:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure  and  who  remains  in  foreclosure  is  about  89  percent  in  the  data  for  2009-2011
31:1148:72243:18:18:72:540:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and is about 88 percent in the model for this period.  The second is that foreclosure delay
31:1149:72334:18:18:72:540:446:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:results in a lower foreclosure rate.  The model foreclosure rate is 9.9 percent for the no delay
31:1150:72430:18:18:72:540:428:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:economy and is 4.5 percent for the foreclosure delay economy.  Although there is no empirical
31:1151:72523:18:17:72:540:410:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:analogue for comparison, given that the no delay economy is a counterfactual, it is interest-
31:1152:72616:17:18:72:540:393:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ing to note, however, that the actual foreclosure rate drops from 8.6 percent in 2001-2003 to
31:1153:72709:18:26:72:200:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:5.5 percent in 2009-2011.
31:1154:72734:26:17:89:539:349:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Foreclosure  delay  also  has  an  impact  on  borrowers’  decisions  to  default  and  to  cure.
31:1155:72831:17:18:72:540:332:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Specifically, borrowers default more frequently and cure more slowly with foreclosure delay.
31:1156:72923:18:18:72:540:314:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The model predicts that the monthly default rate is about 0.3 percentage points (.0105-.0077)
31:1157:73016:18:18:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:higher when there is a 15-month foreclosure timeline (this is roughly a third higher relative
31:1158:73109:18:18:72:540:278:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to the 9-month foreclosure timeline).  Similarly, the cure rate from 90 or more days late to 60
31:1159:73204:18:18:72:540:260:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:days late in the 15-month foreclosure economy drops by about 0.8 percentage points (.1762-
31:1160:73294:18:18:72:540:242:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:.1685).  Since more borrowers default and also remain in the 90 or more days late category
31:1161:73384:18:18:72:540:224:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:longer, they experience more foreclosures.  Thus, with foreclosure delay the foreclosure rate
31:1162:73477:18:18:72:540:206:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rises  roughly  3.8  percentage  points  (.1063-.0675),  which  represents  a  57  percent  increase
31:1163:73577:18:0:72:298:188:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:compared with the economy with no delays.
32:1164:73620:0:33:72:401:730:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:8.2    Quantitative Impact of Foreclosure Delay
32:1165:73667:33:18:72:540:697:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Figures 7 to 11 illustrate the time paths of mortgagor employment, aggregate employment,
32:1166:73755:18:18:72:540:679:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the stock of homes with delinquent mortgages, and the fraction of households with mortgages
32:1167:73846:18:18:72:540:661:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(the  mortgagor  rate)  in  the  three  economies  during  the  experiment.   The  main  finding  is
32:1168:73946:18:18:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:that foreclosure delay considerably affects borrower decisions to default and cure.  This in
32:1169:74038:18:18:72:540:625:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:turn  depresses  employment  but  improves  match  quality  as  unemployed  mortgagors  have
32:1170:74130:18:18:72:540:607:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:additional time to search, which results in higher wages.  As we describe later, the impact
32:1171:74221:18:18:72:540:589:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:from  foreclosure  delay  on  employment  is  equivalent  to  extending  unemployment  benefits
32:1172:74316:18:18:72:540:571:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:between  about  4  months,  which  is  for  the  average  foreclosure  delay  across  all  states,  to
32:1173:74418:18:41:72:398:553:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:about 6 months, which is for the states with the longest delays.
32:1174:74482:41:33:72:376:512:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:8.2.1    Impact of Foreclosure Delay on Employment
32:1175:74532:33:18:72:540:479:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Figure 7 plots employment per capita among mortgagors in the three economies.  We find
32:1176:74618:18:18:72:540:461:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:that mortgagor employment in the economy with the 24-month foreclosure timeline, which
32:1177:74704:18:18:72:540:443:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:characterizes  the  increase  in  foreclosure  delays  that  occurred  in  Florida,  New  York,  New
32:1178:74804:18:18:72:540:425:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Jersey, California, and several other large states, is about 1.3 percentage points lower than
32:1179:74897:18:18:72:540:407:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in the no delay economy.  In levels, the employment rate is about 89.5 percent in the economy
32:1180:74990:18:18:72:540:389:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:with a 9-month foreclosure timeline and about 88.2 percent in the economy with the 24-month
32:1181:75081:18:18:72:540:371:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure  timeline.   Aggregate  employment  in  these  states,  which  combines  mortgagor
32:1182:75175:18:18:72:540:353:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:employment with employment of renters and of homeowners without mortgages, is about 0.5
32:1183:75262:18:18:72:540:335:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:percentage points lower, which reflects the fact that those with mortgages make up roughly
32:1184:75352:18:18:72:540:317:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:43 percent of the model economy’s agents.  The employment rate among mortgagors in the
32:1185:75438:18:17:72:540:299:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:economy with the 15-month foreclosure timeline, which captures the average increase that
32:1186:75526:17:18:72:540:282:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:occurred for all states, and which includes several states with little if any foreclosure delay,
32:1187:75622:18:18:72:540:264:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:is  about  0.75  percentage  points  lower  than  in  the  economy  with  the  9-month  foreclosure
32:1188:75721:18:25:72:449:246:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:timeline, and aggregate employment is about 0.3 percentage points lower.
32:1189:75793:25:18:89:539:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Figure  8  plots  the  differences  in  mortgagor  employment  rates  for  the  three  economies
32:1190:75889:18:18:72:540:203:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in  order  to  highlight  these  differences.   Lemmas  6.1and6.2indicate  why  employment  is
32:1191:75983:18:18:71:539:185:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:lower  when  time  to  foreclose  rises.   Specifically,  the  self-insurance  provided  by  mortgage
32:1192:76084:18:18:71:539:167:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:default results in lower employment as the foreclosure timeline becomes longer.  Thus, longer
32:1193:76177:18:18:71:539:149:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure delay means greater default protection, which in turn means a larger difference in
32:1194:76271:18:18:71:539:131:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:employment between these economies.  Foreclosure delay is a de facto implicit line of credit
32:1195:76363:18:0:71:539:113:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:from  the  lender  to  the  mortgagor,  and  by  extending  the  duration  of  this  credit  line  with
33:1196:76468:0:18:72:540:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure  delays,  this  extra  self-insurance  has  an  impact  on  unemployed  worker  search
33:1197:76566:18:18:72:540:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:decisions  and  reservation  wages.   To  gauge  the  model  relative  to  the  data,  we  note  that
33:1198:76667:18:18:72:540:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:mortgagor employment among PSID respondents drops by about 6 percent between 2007
33:1199:76748:18:18:72:539:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and 2009,  which is of similar magnitude to our experiment.  Appendix16shows that the
33:1200:76833:18:18:72:540:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:drop in employment per capita among mortgagors in the model is consistent with the data.
33:1201:76921:18:18:72:540:640:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Averaging  across  states  with  delays  and  without  delays,  Figure9  plots  the  difference  in
33:1202:77020:18:18:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:aggregate  employment  per  capita,  which  includes  both  mortgagors  and  nonmortgagors  in
33:1203:77114:18:25:72:180:604:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:each model economy.
33:1204:77133:25:18:89:539:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:To  assess  whether our  model produces a  reasonable quantitative impact  of foreclosure
33:1205:77222:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:delay on employment, we measure the impact of changes in unemployment insurance in this
33:1206:77309:18:18:72:539:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:model, given that this topic has been studied considerably.  We do this as inNakajima[2012],
33:1207:77401:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:who constructs a Mortensen-Pissarides model with risk aversion and asset heterogeneity to
33:1208:77490:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:assess the impact of unemployment insurance (UI) extensions on unemployment during the
33:1209:77576:18:17:72:539:489:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:2007-2009 recession.  We find that our model produces anunemployment  benefit  elasticity
33:1210:77665:17:18:72:540:472:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of .43, which is defined as the increase in unemployment durations in weeks resulting from
33:1211:77755:18:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:a  10  percent  increase  in  the  benefit  replacement  rate  for  a  regular  6-month  duration  of
33:1212:77856:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:UI. Unemployment benefit elasticity is commonly referenced in the empirical literature on
33:1213:77945:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:unemployment insurance.Card et al.[2015] provide a summary of this literature and report
33:1214:78033:18:18:72:539:400:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:that this same elasticity measure varies from 0.3 to 2 in U.S. data across several studies.Card
33:1215:78128:18:18:72:539:382:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:et al.[2015] also report measures of this elasticity from data during the Great Recession,
33:1216:78218:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:which range from 0.65 to 0.9.  Our model therefore produces a response of employment to
33:1217:78305:18:25:72:467:346:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:unemployment benefit changes that is on the lower end of existing estimates.
33:1218:78381:25:18:89:539:321:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Since the topic of foreclosure delay and its impact on employment has not been previously
33:1219:78470:18:18:72:540:303:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:studied,  we next place our quantitative estimates in context by calculating the equivalent
33:1220:78561:18:18:72:540:285:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:impact on employment within our model that results from extending unemployment benefits.
33:1221:78649:18:18:72:540:267:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Specifically, we calculate how many additional months of unemployment benefits would result
33:1222:78740:18:18:72:540:249:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in 0.5 percent lower aggregate employment, which is the employment decline in the 24-month
33:1223:78830:18:18:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:timeline economy,  and 0.3 percent lower aggregate employment,  which is the employment
33:1224:78917:18:18:72:540:213:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:decline in the 15-month timeline economy.31We find that the employment decline resulting
33:1225:79005:18:17:72:540:195:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:from  the  24-month  foreclosure  timeline  is  equivalent  to  the  impact  of  about  a  6-month
33:1226:79103:17:18:72:540:178:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:extension of unemployment benefits, and that the employment decline from the 15-month
33:1227:79188:18:18:72:445:160:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure timeline is equivalent to about a 3.7-month benefit extension.
33:1228:79262:18:16:81:539:142:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:31A 24-month UI policy increases the unemployment rate by 1.9 percent.  We simply scale this ratio of UI
33:1229:79366:16:0:72:540:126:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:duration to UR to arrive at our estimates in the paper of the impact of foreclosure delay on unemployment.
34:1230:79474:0:18:89:539:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The employment declines resulting from foreclosure delay are the consequence of different
34:1231:79563:18:18:72:540:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:levels of search intensity and reservation wages, both of which depend on delinquency status.
34:1232:79656:18:18:72:540:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Specifically,  reservation  wages  are  about  4  percent  higher  with  the  24-month  foreclosure
34:1233:79755:18:18:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:timeline compared with the 9-month foreclosure timeline economy at a mortgage payment
34:1234:79840:18:18:72:540:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:delinquency ranging between 1 to 4 months.  Near foreclosure, however, reservation wages
34:1235:79928:18:18:72:540:640:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in both the 9-month timeline economy and the 24-month timeline economy drop by roughly
34:1236:80014:18:18:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:10 percent, and search effort increases as households attempt to find a job quickly in order
34:1237:80106:18:25:72:171:604:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to prevent eviction.
34:1238:80126:25:18:89:539:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Although foreclosure delay does not account for the majority of the decline in U.S. em-
34:1239:80213:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ployment observed since 2008, its relative quantitative impact appears to be similar to several
34:1240:80308:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:other factors that have been studied.  This includes analyses of mismatch employment (Kara-
34:1241:80399:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:han and Rhee [2011],S ̧ahin et al.[2012]), structural changes in the labor market (Charles
34:1242:80489:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:et al.[2013]),  and uncertainty (Schaal[2012]).  All of these papers find that these factors
34:1243:80581:18:17:72:539:489:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:account  for  only  a  modest  amount  of  the  recent  change  in  employment.Fratto  and  Uh-
34:1244:80676:17:18:72:539:472:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:lig[2014]  study  the  impact  of  several  shocks  within  a  single  model  framework,  including
34:1245:80775:18:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:monetary  shocks,  government  spending  shocks,  preference  shocks,  technology  shocks,  and
34:1246:80870:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:wage/price markup shocks, and find that no single factor accounts for more than 2-3 per-
34:1247:80958:18:25:72:335:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:centage points of the recent change in employment.
34:1248:81008:25:18:89:540:393:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Figure10plots the fraction of mortgagors in default in the model economy.  The stock
34:1249:81092:18:18:72:540:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of  mortgages  in  default  reaches  its  maximum  6  quarters  after  the  recession  begins.   The
34:1250:81192:18:18:72:540:357:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:delinquent stock declines thereafter as the economy switches back to the high state.  In the
34:1251:81284:18:18:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:economy with the 24-month foreclosure timeline, delinquencies peak at about 14.2 percent
34:1252:81372:18:18:72:540:321:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of the total stock of mortgages, which is roughly equal to the delinquent stock among the
34:1253:81461:18:18:72:539:303:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:10  most  delayed  states.32The  economy  with  a  15-month  foreclosure  timeline  has  a  peak
34:1254:81557:18:18:72:540:285:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:delinquency  stock  of  11.2  percent,  which  is  modestly  higher  than  the  national  average  of
34:1255:81658:18:18:72:539:267:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:about  10.57  percent.33The  economy  with  the  9-month  foreclosure  timeline,  which  is  the
34:1256:81754:18:18:72:540:249:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:counterfactual, has a peak delinquency stock of about 6 percent.  These large differences in
34:1257:81846:18:18:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the stock of delinquencies are driven by households’ choices to default more frequently and
34:1258:81937:18:18:72:540:213:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:cure more slowly with foreclosure delay.  Empirical work byPace and Zhu[2011] has demon-
34:1259:82025:18:17:72:540:195:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:strated  a  similarly  strong  link  between  delays  and  default.   The  consumption  smoothing
34:1260:82122:17:18:72:540:178:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:motive of default is also consistent with evidence inBaker and Yannelis[2015] andGelman
34:1261:82209:18:19:72:540:160:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:et al.[2015], and it is in line withGuiso et al.[2010] andGerardi et al.[2013], who both find
34:1262:82302:19:12:81:308:141:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:32See McBride [2011] for delinquency rates by state.
34:1263:82354:12:0:81:312:129:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:33Based on LPS data, seeMcBride[2012] for details.
35:1264:82406:0:25:72:276:730:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:very limited roles for strategic default.34
35:1265:82449:25:18:89:539:705:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Figure 11 illustrates the fraction of households with mortgages in each economy.  In the
35:1266:82537:18:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:economy with the 24-month foreclosure timeline, homeownership (with mortgages) drops by
35:1267:82624:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:about 0.5 percentage points, from 42.5 percent to 42.0 percent, 6 quarters after the onset of
35:1268:82717:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the recession, whereas homeownership drops to 41.7 percent over this same time period in
35:1269:82805:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the counterfactual economy with the 9-month foreclosure delay timeline.  Thus, foreclosure
35:1270:82895:18:42:72:381:615:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:delay results in fewer foreclosures and more ultimate curing.
35:1271:82956:42:33:72:368:573:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:8.2.2    Employment and Foreclosure Across States
35:1272:83005:33:18:72:540:540:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The model experiments involving a 24-month timeline, which corresponds to the longest delay
35:1273:83096:18:18:72:540:522:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:states, a 15-month timeline, which corresponds to the U.S. average, and a 9-month timeline,
35:1274:83187:18:18:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:which corresponds to no delay and which is consistent with many states such as Arizona,
35:1275:83274:18:17:72:540:486:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Georgia, Iowa, Texas, and Washington, predict that foreclosure delay reduces employment.
35:1276:83362:17:18:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This section uses the Current Population Survey (CPS) to assess the model’s quantitative
35:1277:83450:18:18:72:540:451:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:results.  To exploit the variation in foreclosure times across states, we categorize households
35:1278:83545:18:18:72:540:433:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:according  to  their  state  and  conduct  a  difference-in-difference  analysis.   Specifically,  we
35:1279:83646:18:18:72:540:415:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:compare employment rates across renters and homeowners in slow and fast foreclosure states,
35:1280:83737:18:18:72:540:397:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:controlling for a host of individual characteristics. We rank states based on the speed at which
35:1281:83833:18:18:72:540:379:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:homeowners transition from foreclosure to liquidation (including REO). Table 9 includes our
35:1282:83924:18:18:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:classification of slow and fast foreclosure states.  We then isolate the top 10 fastest and top
35:1283:84019:18:18:72:540:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:10 slowest foreclosure states in the 2001 through 2013 March Supplement CPS surveys.  We
35:1284:84107:18:18:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:then  compare  employment  status  of  homeowners  and  renters  in  fast  and  slow  foreclosure
35:1285:84204:18:25:72:499:307:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:states, splitting the sample before and after the large increase in foreclosure delays.
35:1286:84291:25:18:89:539:282:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Table  10presents  these  results.   The  dependent  variable  is  a  dummy  variable  if  the
35:1287:84385:18:18:71:539:264:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:household  is  employed,  and  we  include  demographic,  occupation,  and  industry  controls.
35:1288:84480:18:18:71:540:246:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Columns  (1)  and  (2)  of  Table10show  that  homeowners,  as  compared  with  renters,  have
35:1289:84574:18:18:71:539:228:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:a lower employment rate in states with slow foreclosure processes as compared with states
35:1290:84663:18:18:71:539:210:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:with fast foreclosure processes.  The magnitude of this effect ranges between a 0.4 percent
35:1291:84754:18:17:71:539:192:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to a 0.8 percent reduction in employment per capita depending on the control set, which is
35:1292:84844:17:18:71:540:175:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:consistent with the results of our structural model presented Section6.  Columns (3) and
35:1293:84932:18:19:72:540:157:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(4) of Table10split the sample between pre-2007 and post-2007.  We see that the impact
35:1294:85018:19:15:81:539:138:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:34Evidence in Dobbie and Song [2013] about earnings outcomes and debt protection is consistent with our
35:1295:85121:15:0:72:123:123:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:mechanism.
36:1296:85133:0:18:72:540:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of foreclosure delay is weaker in the 2003-2007 period, which is consistent with the fact that
36:1297:85227:18:42:72:468:712:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:there was much less variation in foreclosure time across states in 2003-2007.35
36:1298:85306:42:33:72:339:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:8.2.3    Impact of Foreclosure Delay on Wages
36:1299:85351:33:18:72:540:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Foreclosure delay also affects the quality of jobs that are accepted by the unemployed,  as
36:1300:85442:18:18:72:540:619:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:well as the economy’s wage bill.  Table8 shows that foreclosure delays result in wages that
36:1301:85533:18:18:71:539:601:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:are higher by about 0.2 percent to about 0.3 percent.  The extra self-insurance provided by
36:1302:85624:18:18:71:539:583:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the default protection has two effects:  (i) fewer people are working, which results in a lower
36:1303:85719:18:18:71:539:565:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:employment rate, but those who are working have higher wages.  Table8 indicates that the
36:1304:85807:18:25:71:539:547:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:improved match quality (higher average wages) more than offsets the effect of fewer workers.
36:1305:85899:25:18:89:540:522:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This  result  is  consistent  with  a  large  literature  that  includesEhrenberg  and  Oaxaca
36:1306:85993:18:18:71:539:504:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:[1976],Feldstein  and  Poterba[1984],Addison  and  Blackburn[2000],  andHagedorn  et  al.
36:1307:86082:18:17:71:539:486:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:[2013],  who have found that unemployment insurance extensions improve wage outcomes.
36:1308:86167:17:18:71:539:469:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In  our  model,  we  find  that  unemployed  defaulters  find  jobs  that  pay  0.8  percent  greater
36:1309:86268:18:18:71:539:451:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in a stochastic steady state with the 15-month foreclosure timeline relative to the 9-month
36:1310:86359:18:18:71:539:433:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure timeline. As noted earlier, the 15-month foreclosure timeline is roughly equivalent
36:1311:86454:18:18:71:539:415:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to the 4 month benefit extension, which implies that our wage gains from foreclosure delay
36:1312:86544:18:18:71:539:397:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:are at the lower end of estimates from U.S. data.36Some studies based on European data
36:1313:86630:18:18:71:539:379:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:such  asSchmieder  et  al.[2013]  find  mixed  evidence  regarding  wage  outcomes,  but  other
36:1314:86725:18:18:71:539:361:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:studies such asNekoei et al.[2013], who use Austrian data, find that a UI extension of 9
36:1315:86813:18:25:71:528:343:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:weeks raises re-employment wages by 0.5 percent, which is consistent with our findings.37
36:1316:86902:25:18:89:540:318:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Herkenhoff et al.[2015] provide additional support for the wage findings in this paper.
36:1317:86989:18:18:71:539:300:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:They merge US credit reports and census employment histories to study the impact of credit
36:1318:87079:18:18:71:539:282:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:access on non-employment durations and replacement wages of displaced workers.  They find
36:1319:87168:18:18:71:539:264:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:that credit access is an important source of self-insurance for unemployed households.  They
36:1320:87260:18:12:81:351:246:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:35We thank Sam Schulhofer-Wohl for suggesting this analysis.
36:1321:87320:12:15:81:539:234:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:36Addison and Blackburn [2000] provide a comprehensive survey of the literature, showing that the major-
36:1322:87424:15:12:72:540:219:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:ity of studies that consider the impact of unemployment benefits on re-employment earnings find significant
36:1323:87531:12:12:72:540:207:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:and positive impacts of UI on wages.  The magnitudes vary, and the units of analysis vary, but the general
36:1324:87637:12:8:72:443:195:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:consensus of the literature is that unemployment insurance improves wage outcomes.
36:1325:87719:8:16:81:540:187:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:37The results in Schmieder et al.[2013] are not particularly informative for our study because of large
36:1326:87822:16:12:71:539:171:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:differences in the asset positions of the households we study, and of the 40-42 year old German workers studied
36:1327:87933:12:12:71:539:159:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:inSchmieder et al.[2013].  Specifically, the OECD reports that the German household private savings rate
36:1328:88037:12:12:71:539:147:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:is 10 percent, which suggests that the German households have a significant buffer stock of assets, whereas
36:1329:88144:12:12:71:539:135:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:we documented that the delinquent mortgagors we study have no buffer stock.  Thus, our theory indicates
36:1330:88247:12:0:71:455:123:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:that the impact of UI extensions will be very different across these two different groups.
37:1331:88339:0:18:72:540:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:find that households with greater amounts of unsecured credit, and thus more insurance, take
37:1332:88431:18:18:72:540:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:longer to find jobs, and find higher wage jobs that are in line with the estimates presented
37:1333:88523:18:46:72:97:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:here.
37:1334:88528:46:33:72:540:648:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:8.3    Employment, Delinquency, and Foreclosure:  Model and Data
37:1335:88592:33:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Figure 12 shows the model’s employment per capita by delinquency status for the 15-month
37:1336:88680:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:timeline economy.  Employment rises in the model as delinquencies rise, with borrowers rais-
37:1337:88772:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ing their search intensity and reducing their reservation wages.  The mortgagor employment
37:1338:88862:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rate in the model rises by about 5 percent between being 60 days late and being in the fore-
37:1339:88954:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:closure process.  This increase in the model’s mortgagor employment rate is smoother than
37:1340:89043:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the increase in the data, in which the latter is characterized by an increase that primarily
37:1341:89135:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:occurs for mortgagors who are in the foreclosure process.  The increase in the employment
37:1342:89224:18:25:72:294:489:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rate in the actual data is about 10 percent.
37:1343:89268:25:18:89:539:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:There are two likely reasons why the model employment increase is smoother than the
37:1344:89351:18:18:72:540:446:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:increases displayed in Figures 1 and 2 from the PSID and the SCF, and is also not as large
37:1345:89441:18:18:72:540:428:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:as in those data.  One reason is that our model, like all standard search models, does not
37:1346:89531:18:17:72:540:410:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:produce as many long-term unemployed as in the data.  This is because unemployment in
37:1347:89616:17:18:72:540:393:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:standard  search  models  is  Markovian.   This  means  that  search  models  generate  very  few
37:1348:89713:18:18:72:540:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:individuals who are unemployed for long periods of time (e.g.,  more than a few months),
37:1349:89801:18:18:72:540:357:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:whereas 45 percent of the unemployed between 2009 and 2011 were unemployed for longer
37:1350:89886:18:18:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:than 6 months.  We are unaware of any models that are capable of producing this share of
37:1351:89974:18:25:72:209:321:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:long duration unemployed.
37:1352:89999:25:18:89:539:296:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Another reason is that there is no heterogeneity in the flow utility derived from housing
37:1353:90088:18:18:72:540:278:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in our model.  This means that the opportunity cost of eviction is identical for all borrowers.
37:1354:90183:18:18:72:540:260:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:However,  it is likely that there are some households who are very strongly attached (well
37:1355:90273:18:18:72:540:242:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:matched) to their homes, and who choose to prevent eviction even at a very high cost.  This
37:1356:90364:18:0:72:222:224:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:is not included in this model.
38:1357:90396:0:27:72:540:730:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:9    Sensitivity  Analyses:  Wage  Ladders  and  Extended
38:1358:90453:27:37:101:318:703:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:Unemployment Insurance
38:1359:90475:37:18:72:540:666:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This section considers the sensitivity of the results to two changes to the benchmark model:
38:1360:90567:18:18:72:540:648:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(i) wage ladders as inLjungqvist and Sargent[1998] and (ii) unemployment insurance ex-
38:1361:90653:18:46:72:116:630:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:tensions.
38:1362:90662:46:33:72:209:584:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:9.1    Wage Ladders
38:1363:90681:33:18:72:540:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This  section  reports  findings  for  the  case  of  a  wage  ladder,  rather  than  the  fixed  wage
38:1364:90783:18:18:72:540:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:contract.  The impact of foreclosure delay is similar to that with fixed wages.  Figure13shows
38:1365:90877:18:18:71:539:515:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the difference in employment per capita between the economy with a 15-month foreclosure
38:1366:90964:18:18:71:539:497:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:timeline and the economy with a 9-month foreclosure timeline under different assumptions
38:1367:91052:18:18:71:539:479:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:about on-the-job wage growth.  From SIPP data, we calculate that the probability of a wage
38:1368:91142:18:18:71:539:461:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:increase of at least $1 per month is about 4.66 percent.38This measure includes transitory
38:1369:91232:18:18:71:539:443:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:wage changes, so we take this as an upper bound on the rate at which a worker may climb
38:1370:91319:18:18:71:539:425:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the  wage  ladder.   Prior  studies  such  asLjungqvist  and  Sargent[1998]  indirectly  inferred
38:1371:91416:18:18:71:539:407:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:this parameter, and if we use their values for wage growth, the model results remain largely
38:1372:91508:18:18:71:540:389:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:unchanged.  As Figure13shows, the difference in employment rates between the 24-month
38:1373:91593:18:18:72:540:371:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure timeline relative to the 9-month foreclosure timeline is about 0.1 percentage points
38:1374:91689:18:46:72:208:353:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:smaller with wage ladders.
38:1375:91715:46:33:72:351:307:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:9.2    Extended Unemployment Benefits
38:1376:91752:33:17:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Next,  to  assess  the  relative  importance  of  foreclosure  delays  in  an  environment  with  ex-
38:1377:91853:17:18:72:540:257:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:tended unemployment benefits,  we compare our benchmark model with a model in which
38:1378:91936:18:18:72:539:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment insurance lasts for 2 years (in expectation).  The impact on thesteady state
38:1379:92025:18:18:72:540:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of the economy from a 2-year permanent benefit extension is to raise the unemployment rate
38:1380:92115:18:18:72:539:203:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:by 1.9 percent.  This increase in unemployment is nearly identical to that found inNakajima
38:1381:92206:18:16:81:539:185:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:38See Appendix 13for the full transition matrix.  We use the SIPP-constructed wage rate “wage,” which
38:1382:92307:16:12:72:540:169:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:is described as the “Hourly rate this month” deflated by the CPI. The gross probability reported earlier is
38:1383:92414:12:12:72:540:157:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:the average probability of transiting up the wage ladder by $1 or more in any given month.  If we calculate
38:1384:92521:12:12:72:540:145:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:net wage increases, i.e.  we subtract from this measure the probability of going down at least $1 or more, the
38:1385:92631:12:11:72:540:133:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:transition probability is 1.36 percent.  If we further isolate permanent changes, this number declines further
38:1386:92741:11:0:72:457:122:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:and the fixed contract model becomes a closer approximation to the wage ladder model.
39:1387:92828:0:18:72:540:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:[2012] (Table 4 of his paper) who also considers a 2-year permanent benefit extension but in
39:1388:92920:18:18:72:540:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:a Mortensen-Pissarides style model.  AsNakajima[2012] discusses, this magnitude response
39:1389:93008:18:18:72:540:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:is consistent with UI studies such asKatz and Meyer[1990],Chetty[2008],Rothstein[2011]
39:1390:93094:18:18:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:andHagedorn  et  al.[2013].  To complete  the sensitivity  analysis,  Figure14demonstrates
39:1391:93184:18:18:72:540:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:that the impact of foreclosure delay on employment in the economy with a 2-year benefit
39:1392:93271:18:52:72:501:640:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:extension is only about 0.05 percentage points weaker than under the baseline case.
39:1393:93354:52:37:72:329:588:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:10    Summary and Conclusion
39:1394:93382:37:18:72:540:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This paper documents the fact that mortgage default as well as the home foreclosure process
39:1395:93473:18:18:72:540:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:are persistent and reversible states, as homeowners who enter mortgage default often remain
39:1396:93564:18:18:72:540:515:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in default for a long period of time, and that these same homeowners often exit default or
39:1397:93654:18:18:72:540:497:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:cure even when they have entered the foreclosure process.  To our knowledge, the persistence
39:1398:93746:18:18:72:540:479:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of default and foreclosure,  and the frequent curing from these states,  are absent from the
39:1399:93838:18:18:72:540:461:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:literature.  We also present evidence from the PSID and the SCF that mortgage default is
39:1400:93926:18:18:72:540:443:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:associated  with  job  acceptance,  as  the  employment  rate  among  delinquent  mortgagors  in
39:1401:94022:18:25:72:540:425:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure is higher than that for delinquent mortgagors who have yet to enter foreclosure.
39:1402:94114:25:18:89:539:400:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We construct a labor search model with homeownership that structurally interprets these
39:1403:94201:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:facts as unemployed households using mortgage default as a means to help smooth consump-
39:1404:94289:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:tion and search for a high-paying job, and who accept jobs to exit foreclosure when eviction is
39:1405:94384:18:18:72:540:346:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:imminent.  Our main finding is that the large increase in time to foreclose in some U.S. states
39:1406:94479:18:18:72:540:328:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in which foreclosure required about two years, including New York, New Jersey, and Florida
39:1407:94569:18:17:72:540:310:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(among others),  reduced the employment rate of homeowners with mortgages by 1.3 per-
39:1408:94654:17:18:72:540:293:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:cent and reduced total employment within these states by about 0.5 percent.  To assess the
39:1409:94744:18:18:72:540:275:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:plausibility of this impact, we conducted a difference-in-difference estimate of employment
39:1410:94835:18:18:72:540:257:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rates between homeowners and renters across states and find that homeowner employment
39:1411:94920:18:18:72:540:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rates were between 0.4 percent to 0.8 percent lower.  The model also predicts that foreclo-
39:1412:95011:18:18:72:540:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:sure delay of 15 months (the national average) increases the stock of delinquent loans by 45
39:1413:95103:18:18:72:540:203:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:percent, resulting from longer foreclosure processing time and slower mortgagor curing.  To
39:1414:95194:18:18:72:540:185:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:put the model’s prediction in context, our results indicate that a 15-month increase in the
39:1415:95285:18:18:72:540:167:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure timeline has an impact on the aggregate economy roughly equal to a 6-month
39:1416:95371:18:25:72:241:149:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:unemployment benefit extension.
39:1417:95402:25:0:89:539:124:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The  model  also  predicts  an  increase  in  match  quality,  as  foreclosure  delay  results  in
40:1418:95502:0:18:72:540:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:longer unemployment spells, which allows the unemployed to wait for higher-wage jobs.  We
40:1419:95591:18:18:72:540:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:find  that  the  wage  bill  in  the  economy  with  foreclosure  delay  rises  by  about  0.3  percent.
40:1420:95695:18:18:72:540:694:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This positive analysis of foreclosure delay provides an input to policymaking discussions on
40:1421:95787:18:18:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:alternative approaches in providing additional insurance to homeowners during periods of
40:1422:95875:18:62:72:287:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:substantial job loss and mortgage default.
40:1423:95917:62:25:72:163:596:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:References

56:1797:116174:33:18:72:539:603:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f2:PSID Sample:2009-2011 PSID Core/Immigrant Sample, Working-Age Heads with Mort-
56:1798:116252:18:25:72:403:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:gages (or Previously Had a Mortgage but was Foreclosed Upon).
56:1799:116313:25:18:89:539:560:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:When computing employment rates across delinquency status, we must control for com-
56:1800:116396:18:18:72:540:542:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:position.  For example,  it may be the case that those who are in foreclosure also work in
56:1801:116486:18:18:72:540:524:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:lower-paying jobs and therefore have better employment prospects since the labor market is
56:1802:116576:18:18:72:540:506:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:polarized.  We control for basic differences across households in Tables 2 and 3.  We estimate
56:1803:116670:18:43:72:217:488:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:regressions of the basic form
56:1804:116699:43:33:138:473:445:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:I(employedt) =β0+β1delinquentt+β2foreclosuret+β3Xt+-t.
56:1805:116753:33:18:89:540:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The  controlsXtinclude  basic  demographic  controls  for  age,  sex,  marital  status,  and
56:1806:116845:18:18:72:540:394:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:education as well as income and asset controls, and state level controls for foreclosure pro-
56:1807:116938:18:18:72:540:376:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:cedures.  Table 1 illustrates employment per capita across delinquency status and states for
56:1808:117030:18:46:72:129:358:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:both years.
56:1809:117041:46:33:72:323:312:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:11.2    SCF Composition Correction
56:1810:117075:33:18:72:540:279:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f2:SCF Sample:2007-2009 SCF Sample, Working-Age Heads with Mortgages (or Previously
56:1811:117155:18:25:72:296:261:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Had a Mortgage but was Foreclosed Upon).
56:1812:117195:25:18:89:540:236:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We follow the same exact procedure with the SCF to correct for composition.  Table4
56:1813:117278:18:18:72:540:218:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:reports both the OLS (Columns (1) and (2)) and Logit (Columns (3) and (4)) results used
56:1814:117365:18:17:72:540:200:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to construct the composition corrected employment per capita by delinquency in the main

57:1816:117459:0:37:72:368:730:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:12    Spousal Employment Patterns
57:1817:117492:37:18:72:540:693:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Using the same methodology as Appendix 11, Table11illustrates a similar pattern of in-
57:1818:117578:18:18:72:540:675:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:creasing employment among spouses who are in foreclosure.  The dependent variable is an
57:1819:117665:18:18:72:540:657:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:indicator  if  the  head’s  spouse  is  employed.   Columns  (1)  and  (2)  include  all  heads,  and
57:1820:117766:18:18:72:540:639:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Columns (3) and (4) only include married heads.  Column (1) shows that relative to spouses
57:1821:117856:18:18:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:who have a head of household that is current on the mortgage, spouses who are 90+ days
57:1822:117942:18:18:72:540:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:late are 7.8% less likely to be employed.  However, relative to spouses who have a head of
57:1823:118032:18:18:72:540:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:household that is current on the mortgage, spouses in foreclosure are only 1.9% less likely
57:1824:118123:18:18:72:540:567:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to be employed.  One possible interpretation of these correlations is that both the head and
57:1825:118215:18:32:72:342:549:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the spouse seek jobs in order to stave off foreclosure.

58:1852:119457:0:27:72:547:730:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:13    Computational Details, Wage Offer Distribution and
58:1853:119513:27:37:110:354:703:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:Aggregate Transition Matrix
58:1854:119540:37:18:72:540:666:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We solved the dynamic programming problem by using value function iteration over a discrete
58:1855:119631:18:18:72:540:648:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:state space.  The grid for search effort is evenly spaced over the interval [0,1] with 21 nodes.

61:1922:122620:34:18:71:539:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f2:Proof.Consider  an  unemployed  agent  that  is  comparing  the  options  of  (i)  turning  down

61:1924:122815:18:18:71:539:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to  default,  versus  (ii)  accepting  a  wage  draw  equal  to  their  reservation  wage  and  paying
61:1925:122917:18:18:71:540:515:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:current.   Suppressing  the  state  space,  denote  the  reservation  wagew∗(b)  =w∗i(b,a,n;θ).

63:2079:126156:38:0:136:154:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f8:0<

63:2090:126209:16:0:399:413:553:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:∂ψ

63:2092:126217:34:18:72:540:527:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The intuition behind the inequality is that the effect of protection is strongest for those who

63:2094:126413:18:18:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:reservation wage is at least the benefit amount, thus for all the wages above the reservation
63:2095:126506:18:0:72:242:473:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:wage, the above inequality holds.
64:2096:126541:0:37:72:298:730:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:15    Cash-Out Refinancing
64:2097:126567:37:18:72:540:693:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:As shown in Figure16, the cash-out refinancing mortgage market collapsed during the 2007-
64:2098:126656:18:18:72:540:675:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:2009  recession  in  the  United  States.   Large  declines  in  home  equity  along  with  tightened
64:2099:126757:18:35:72:516:657:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:lending standards led to the 5 fold reduction in cash out refinancing mortgage volume.
64:2100:126843:35:352:180:428:622:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Figure 16:  Cash-Out Refinancing (Source:  LPS)
64:2101:126890:352:37:72:483:270:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:16    Employment Per Capita among Mortgagors
64:2102:126934:37:18:72:540:233:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:As shown in Figure17, the 2007-2009 recession in the United States is marked by a record
64:2103:127022:18:18:72:540:215:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:number of non-employed mortgagors and a record number of delinquent mortgagors.40Em-
64:2104:127106:18:18:71:539:197:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ployment  per  capita  drops  by  more  than  6  percent  between  2007  and  2009  and  remains
64:2105:127202:18:18:71:539:179:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:depressed through 2011 (the last year plotted).  The magnitude of this record reduction in
64:2106:127292:18:18:71:340:161:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:employment per capita is consistent with our model.
64:2107:127343:18:15:81:539:143:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:40The  image  includes  several  data  sources  including  the  Panel  Study  of  Income  Dynamics  (PSID)  up
64:2108:127453:15:12:72:540:128:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:to the most recent publicly available survey in 2011, Lender Processing Services Data (LPS) through 2011,
64:2109:127558:12:0:72:540:116:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:CoreLogic House Price Data through 2011, and the National Bureau of Economic Research (NBER) business
65:2110:127661:0:320:164:444:723:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Figure 17:  Mortgagor Employment Per Capita (PSID)
65:2111:127711:320:37:72:405:403:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:17    Institutional Details of Foreclosure
65:2112:127753:37:18:72:540:366:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This section provides background information on the way mortgage default and foreclosure
65:2113:127841:18:18:72:540:348:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:typically work.  It is important to note that there is considerable variability across servicers
65:2114:127937:18:25:72:303:330:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and states as to how they handle foreclosure.
65:2115:127982:25:18:89:539:305:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The  order  of  events  in  a  foreclosure  has  potential  to  distort  buyers’  incentives  to  pay
65:2116:128083:18:18:72:540:287:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:since foreclosure is a slow and relatively predictable process.  The usual order of events is as
65:2117:128179:18:38:72:110:269:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:follows:
65:2118:128187:38:28:86:362:231:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:1.  Miss payments (30+ days late, Enter Delinquency)
65:2119:128239:28:27:86:292:203:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:2.  Notice of Default (Enter Foreclosure)
65:2120:128280:27:28:86:351:176:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:3.  Notice of Sale (1 month prior to foreclosure sale)
65:2121:128334:28:24:86:274:148:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:4.  Foreclosure Auction (Sheriff Sale)
65:2122:128372:24:0:72:122:124:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:cycle dates.
66:2123:128386:0:28:86:144:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:5.  Eviction
66:2124:128398:28:28:86:492:702:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:6.PotentialDeficiency Judgment if Sale Price<Remaining Mortgage Balance
66:2125:128469:28:38:86:461:674:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:7.  Ineligible for government-backed loans for 7 years (seeLowrey[2010]).
66:2126:128542:38:18:89:539:636:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Legally, if a mortgagor breaks the terms of the mortgage, the bank can ask for the entire
66:2127:128631:18:18:71:539:618:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:debt  to  be  paid  immediately.   If  the  mortgagor  cannot  pay  this  entire  amount,  the  bank
66:2128:128731:18:18:71:539:600:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:can foreclose.  There are two main types of foreclosures in the United States:  judicial and
66:2129:128823:18:18:71:540:582:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:nonjudicial (seeGhent and Kudlyak[2011] for state classifications).  To complete a judicial
66:2130:128914:18:18:71:539:564:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure,  the  bank  that  owns  the  mortgage  must  sue  the  person  living  in  the  home  in
66:2131:129015:18:18:71:539:546:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:a state court.  A judge is required to rule on the case before a foreclosure sale can occur.
66:2132:129107:18:18:71:539:528:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A  foreclosure  sale  is  called  a  “sheriff  sale.”   A  non-judicial  foreclosure,  also  known  as  a
66:2133:129212:18:18:71:539:510:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:foreclosure by power of sale, allows the bank to sell the house without the court’s approval.
66:2134:129305:18:17:71:539:492:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A notice of default explains that the bank intends to sell the property and that if the debt
66:2135:129397:17:18:71:539:475:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:is not cured, there will be a public auction for the house.  A notice of sale is issued 1 month
66:2136:129492:18:18:71:539:457:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:prior  to  the  foreclosure  auction  date.   If  the  bank  is  unable  to  sell  the  home  in  a  public
66:2137:129599:18:18:71:539:439:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:auction, which means “no acceptable bids are made,” or the bank bids for the house itself,
66:2138:129689:18:25:71:539:421:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:then the house becomes owned by the bank.  The term for this is “real estate owned” (REO).
66:2139:129779:25:18:89:539:396:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:It is possible to temporarily postpone the foreclosure process by bankruptcy (however
66:2140:129864:18:18:71:539:378:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the courts cannot modify loans) or by challenging the banks’ right to the property they are
66:2141:129955:18:18:71:539:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:trying to foreclose upon.41One component of the recent robo-signing scandal has to do with
66:2142:130045:18:25:71:478:342:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the banks’ inability to prove that they had the right of interest in the property.
66:2143:130127:25:18:89:539:317:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Regardless of the foreclosure procedure, each state has laws about recourse and nonre-
66:2144:130213:18:18:71:539:299:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:course  loans.   In  a  state  with  recourse,  selling  a  home  for  less  than  the  amount  due  may
66:2145:130317:18:18:71:539:281:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:result in a deficiency judgment.  Deficiency judgments mandate that the borrower pay the
66:2146:130405:18:18:71:539:263:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:difference between the sale price and the amount owed on the mortgage.  Many mortgages
66:2147:130491:18:18:71:539:245:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:however are nonrecourse loans,  meaning that the bank cannot sue to obtain the assets of
66:2148:130579:18:18:71:539:227:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the person who held the mortgage.  As a result, in most cases, borrowers are exempt from
66:2149:130667:18:18:71:539:209:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:deficiency judgments.  In California, for instance, the first purchase-money mortgage for a
66:2150:130758:18:18:71:539:191:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:residential property is a nonrecourse loan.  However, the state laws are not entirely uniform
66:2151:130851:18:25:71:438:173:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:across all mortgages, e.g.  all refinanced loans in California are recourse.
66:2152:130927:25:18:89:539:148:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:There is also a chance for homeowners to ‘redeem’ their homes after foreclosure if they
66:2153:131014:18:15:81:540:130:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:41For more on bankruptcy and foreclosure, see Li and White[2009],Luzzetti and Neumuller[2012], and
66:2154:131112:15:0:72:134:115:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Mitman[2011]
67:2155:131126:0:18:72:540:730:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:are able to raise enough money.  These redemption periods can last up to a year and vary
67:2156:131214:18:0:72:116:712:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:by state.
